Not a duplicate of bugs #4, #79, #89 (those addressed search-panel latency, deferred indexing, and SQLite `WALMode` respectively ŌĆö none moved `ModelContainer` creation off the main thread).
**Fix**: Move `ModelContainer` creation to a background task or use `Task.detached` to initialize the container off the main thread, then inject it asynchronously into the app's environment. Alternatively, investigate whether SwiftData's `ModelContainer` init can be made lazy or cached across reinstalls. GH: #633

### Bug #185 ŌĆö AI provider editor: Base URL field has no guidance about what path the app appends ŌĆö users enter full endpoint URL, causing double-path construction and silent failure (REPORTED 2026-05-14)

**Repro**: Settings ŌåÆ AI ŌåÆ Providers ŌåÆ add or edit a provider ŌåÆ observe the Base URL field.
**Expected**: The field explains what URL format to enter ŌĆö specifically, whether to include the endpoint path or just the base.
**Actual**: Placeholder text is `"https://api.example.com/v1"` (gives a format hint) but no text explains that the app appends `/chat/completions` for OpenAI-compatible or `/v1/messages` for Anthropic. Users entering `https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions` (the full endpoint) will have the app construct `https://openrouter.ai/api/v1/chat/completions/chat/completions` ŌĆö this 404s or returns a confusing error from the provider with no explanation in the UI.
**Root cause** (`AIProviderEditSheet+Sections.swift:68`): placeholder is `"https://api.example.com/v1"` only; no footer text; no per-kind dynamic hint. In `AIProvider.swift:119` (OpenAI-compat): `baseURL.appendingPathComponent("chat/completions")`; in `AnthropicProvider.swift:134`: `baseURL.appendingPathComponent("v1/messages")`. Correct values:
- OpenAI-compatible (e.g. OpenRouter): `https://openrouter.ai/api/v1`
- Anthropic: `https://api.anthropic.com`
**Fix**: Add a `Section` footer or `Text` hint below the Base URL field that updates dynamically with the selected `kind`, e.g. "Enter the base URL ŌĆö the app will call `/chat/completions` from this base." + a pre-filled example per known provider. Optionally detect if the user has typed a URL that already ends in `/chat/completions` or `/messages` and warn. GH: #627

### Bug #184 ŌĆö Add Provider: "Save Key" and "Test Connection" always disabled ŌĆö buttons visible but non-functional, explanation buried in tiny caption text (REPORTED 2026-05-14)

**Repro**: Settings ŌåÆ AI ŌåÆ Providers ŌåÆ "+" (add new provider) ŌåÆ fill in Name + Base URL ŌåÆ observe "Save Key" and "Test Connection" buttons.
**Expected**: User can save their API key and test the connection while creating a new provider.
**Actual**: Both buttons are disabled (greyed out) in add-mode. "Save Key" is `.disabled(apiKey.isEmpty || existing == nil)` ŌĆö always disabled when `existing == nil` (add-mode). "Test Connection" is `.disabled(testInFlight || !isAPIKeySaved || existing == nil)` ŌĆö also always disabled in add-mode. The explanation ("Enter your API key above, then tap Save to create the profile" / "Save the profile first to test the connection") is rendered in `caption2`/`tertiary` ŌĆö tiny, low-contrast text that users routinely miss. User believes the buttons are broken.
**Root cause** (`AIProviderEditSheet+Sections.swift:145, 185`): Intentional design decision (audit round-1 fix [4]) to prevent keychain orphans: in add-mode the sheet generates a UUID up front but the profile isn't yet in the store. Writing a keychain entry via "Save Key" then tapping Cancel would leak an orphaned secret. The fix addresses the underlying concern correctly but presents two permanently-disabled visible buttons with insufficient explanation.
**Fix options**: (a) hide "Save Key" button entirely in add-mode ŌĆö replace with inline note "Your API key will be saved when you tap Save above"; (b) hide "Test Connection" section in add-mode or promote the explanation to body-weight text; (c) allow "Save Key" in add-mode using an ephemeral keychain entry that's deleted on Cancel (architectural change). Option (a)+(b) is the cheapest correct fix. GH: #625

### Bug #183 ŌĆö TXT search panel freezes UI on first open ŌĆö enqueueBookIndexing runs on @MainActor, blocking main thread during file I/O + encoding detection (REPORTED 2026-05-14)

**Repro**: Open any large TXT file (e.g. 5MB+ CJK novel) ŌåÆ tap the search icon ŌåÆ UI freezes for several seconds before the search panel appears.
**Expected**: Search panel opens immediately; indexing/extraction runs in the background.
**Actual**: Main thread blocks during text extraction + encoding detection; UI is unresponsive until extraction completes. Already-indexed books are not affected (first-open only).
**Root cause** (`ReaderSearchCoordinator.swift`): The class is annotated `@MainActor` (line 12). `enqueueBookIndexing` is a `private static func` with no `nonisolated` keyword ŌåÆ inherits `@MainActor`. At line 142-143 it calls `let result = try await extractor.extractWithOffsets(from: fileURL)` ŌĆö `TXTTextExtractor.extractWithOffsets()` is `async` but its body calls `Self.decodeFile(at:)` synchronously: `Data(contentsOf: url, options: .mappedIfSafe)` + `TXTService.decodeForDisplayAndSearch()` (encoding detection). Both are blocking. `BackgroundIndexingCoordinator` uses `Task.detached(priority: .background)` for FTS5 indexing, but only AFTER extraction ŌĆö extraction still blocks main. Not a duplicate of #4 (VM creation), #79 (deferred indexing), #89 (SQLite open) ŌĆö those addressed different performance seams without moving text extraction off the main thread.
**Fix**: Mark `enqueueBookIndexing` as `nonisolated` and wrap the extraction call in `Task.detached(priority: .utility)`, or move extraction to a dedicated non-isolated async method inside `TXTTextExtractor`. GH: #623

### Bug #182 ŌĆö EPUB search: cross-chapter result tap navigates but shows no yellow highlight (FIXED 2026-05-18)

**Repro**: Open any multi-chapter EPUB ŌåÆ tap search ŌåÆ type a word that appears in a chapter other than the current one ŌåÆ tap the result.
**Expected**: Reader navigates to the correct chapter and paints a temporary yellow background on the matched word for ~3 seconds.
**Actual**: Reader navigates to the correct chapter (top) but no yellow highlight is visible. User cannot locate the matched text without manually scanning the page.
**Same-chapter searches work** ŌĆö if the match is already in the loaded chapter, `window.find()` succeeds and the highlight is visible.
**Root cause** (`EPUBWebViewBridge.swift`, `updateUIView`): When a cross-chapter search result is tapped, `contentURL` and `pendingHighlightJS` are set in the same SwiftUI state update. In `updateUIView`, `webView.loadFileURL(contentURL, ...)` is called (starts async load) and then `evaluateJavaScript(pendingHighlightJS)` is called immediately on the same call stack ŌĆö before the new chapter DOM is ready. `window.find()` runs on the old/loading page, returns false, no `<span>` is injected. `onPendingJSCompleted()` then clears `pendingHighlightJS`. When `webView(_:didFinish:)` fires later with the correct DOM, `pendingHighlightJS` is already nil. The `onPageDidFinishLoad` callback only calls `restoreHighlightsOnLoad` (persisted highlights), never the search highlight. Contrast: `pendingScrollFraction` is stored in the coordinator and consumed in `didFinish` ŌĆö `pendingHighlightJS` needs the same deferred treatment.
**Fix**: Store the search quote and progression in the coordinator at URL-change time; consume in `webView(_:didFinish:)` after theme CSS and pagination/scroll setup, analogous to `pendingScrollFraction`. GH: #621

**Round-2 + round-3 (2026-05-15 ŌåÆ 2026-05-18):** round-1's deferred-eval mechanism landed but the symptom persisted. Round-2 found the `Locator.textQuote` passed to `window.find()` was the raw search snippet (`...prefix<b>match</b>suffix...`) ŌĆö `SearchHitToLocatorResolver.cleanSnippetForTextQuote` now strips the `<b>`/`...` markup. Round-3 found the residual cause: `EPUBHighlightBridge.searchHighlightJS` ran `window.find()` exactly once, synchronously at `webView(_:didFinish:)` ŌĆö before the freshly-loaded chapter finishes its post-load relayout (foliate-js `cssPreprocessJS`, a `WKUserScript` injected `atDocumentEnd`, rewrites every `-epub-*`/`page-break-*` rule), so `window.find()` returns false and no `.vreader_search_highlight` span is created. Verify-cron round-5 DOM-probes confirmed the span is never injected via the user-tap pipeline. **Round-3 fix** (`searchHighlightJS`, JS-only ŌĆö the Swift stashŌåÆconsume pipeline was already correct): poll `window.find()` on a bounded 50ms retry loop (40 attempts Ōēł 2s) until the rendered DOM is searchable; a `window.__vreaderSearchHighlightGen` generation token supersedes concurrent retry loops; the wrap-and-insert is `try/catch`-guarded. Codex audit `019e3959` (3 rounds, 1 Medium + 4 Low all fixed, ship-as-is): `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-621-epub-cross-chapter-highlight-r3-audit.md`.

### Bug #181 ŌĆö TXT/MD Add Note: annotated text not highlighted after saving note (FIXED 2026-05-14)

**Repro**: Open any TXT or MD file ŌåÆ long-press word ŌåÆ tap "Add Note" ŌåÆ type text ŌåÆ tap Save ŌåÆ modal dismisses.
**Expected**: Selected text shows a yellow (or tinted) background highlight indicating an annotation is attached.
**Actual**: Text appears identical to surrounding text ŌĆö no visual indicator. Note IS saved and appears in Annotations panel.
**Root cause** (`ReaderNotificationModifier.swift:108-113`): `onSave` calls `addAnnotation()` (creates `AnnotationRecord`) only ŌĆö no `highlightCoordinator.create(...)` call, so annotation range never enters `persistedHighlightRanges`. Contrast: EPUB's `handleHighlightWithNote` calls `coordinator.create(..., note:)` ŌåÆ creates `HighlightRecord` that IS rendered.
**Context**: Feature #4 criterion 8c was cross-referenced to bug #160 but bug #160 (HighlightRecord chapter-mode rendering) is architecturally separate from this gap (annotation save never creates a HighlightRecord). Affects both TXT and MD. **FIXED via `handleAnnotationSave` now persisting both an `AnnotationRecord` (for the Notes panel) AND a `HighlightRecord` with `note: trimmed` (for the yellow highlight on the text). `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleAnnotationSave` gained a `highlightCoordinator: HighlightCoordinator` parameter; the inline `onSave` closure in `ReaderNotificationModifier` now delegates to the canonical handler (eliminates duplication that caused the gap in the first place). Atomicity: `addAnnotation` is now invoked under explicit `do/catch` ŌĆö if it throws, the function returns before `coordinator.create(...)` so the two records stay in lockstep (audit-driven addition). pendingAnnotationInfo is cleared BEFORE the awaits inside the handler so the AddNoteSheet dismisses immediately on Save; MainActor serialization guarantees re-entrancy safety (a second queued save Task observes `pendingAnnotationInfo = nil` and bails before doing any work). Codex MCP audit `019e251f` (2 rounds): round 1 found 1 High (dual-write atomicity), 2 Medium (existing-highlight + Add Note drops note via dedupe ŌĆö accepted as separate follow-up bug; re-entrancy from rapid taps ŌĆö accepted as effectively-safe via MainActor serialization), 1 Low (file size). High fix applied with regression test; Medium #2 deferred (pre-existing PersistenceActor.addHighlight dedupe behavior, not introduced here); Medium #3 accepted with rationale documented. Round 2: zero new findings, ship-as-is. Test gate: 15/15 ReaderNotificationHandlers tests pass including 3 new bug #181 regression tests (`handleAnnotationSave_alsoCreatesHighlightRecord_bug181`, `handleAnnotationSave_annotationPersistenceFails_skipsHighlight_bug181`, `handleAnnotationSave_locatorFactoryFailure_skipsBoth_bug181`). Pre-FIXED verify: the bug-181 regression test ran with the pre-fix logic would fail (`storeAddCount == 0` and `renderer.appliedRecords.isEmpty` ŌĆö no HighlightRecord persisted, no apply() call). With the fix, both assertions hold (`storeAddCount == 1`, `appliedRecords.count == 1`, applied.color == "yellow", applied.note == "remember this"). Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-616-txt-md-add-note-no-highlight-audit.md`. Follow-up filed informally (track as bug or feature on next triage cycle): "Add Note on already-highlighted TXT/MD range should update note on existing HighlightRecord (currently dedupe returns existing record unchanged)". GH: #616

### Bug #180 ŌĆö TXT scroll mode must scroll continuously + smoothly across chapters ŌĆö REOPENED + RE-SCOPED 2026-05-16: abandon discrete chapter-swap, render one continuous surface (FIXED 2026-05-15, REOPENED 2026-05-16)

**Original symptom (FIXED 2026-05-15, commit 5f75fde / PR #681)**: In TXT scroll mode, scrolling to a chapter boundary just bounced ŌĆö the user had to reveal chrome and tap "Next chapter". Fixed by adding `didScrollPastBottomBoundary()` / `didScrollPastTopBoundary()` to `TXTTextViewBridgeDelegate`, boundary detection in `TXTTextViewBridgeCoordinator.sendScrollPosition`, and `TXTReaderViewModel.goToNextChapter()` / `goToPreviousChapter()`. Codex audit `019e2923`; 7 tests in `TXTScrollBoundaryChapterNavTests.swift`.

**REOPENED 2026-05-16**: User reports the fix made scroll-mode reading worse. After the fix, scrolling is discontinuous ŌĆö it jumps to the **end** of the next chapter, then jumps again, cascading through chapters; it never scrolls smoothly and lands in the wrong place.

**Repro (REOPENED)**: Open any multi-chapter TXT file ŌåÆ Layout = Scroll ŌåÆ scroll down toward the end of Chapter 1. **Actual**: instead of advancing to the *top* of Chapter 2, the view jumps to the *end* of Chapter 2 (or further), repeatedly. **Expected**: advancing a chapter lands at the top of the new chapter and scrolling stays smooth.

**Root cause (REOPENED)**: The #180 fix swaps the entire chapter text on boundary but never resets the scroll view's `contentOffset`:
1. `TXTReaderViewModel.navigateToChapter` (`TXTReaderViewModel.swift:363-401`) sets `currentChapterLocalUTF16 = 0` in the model but does NOT push a scroll-to-top command to the bridge.
2. `TXTTextViewBridge.updateUIView` restores scroll only via the `scrollToOffset` path, which is `nil` after a boundary-triggered chapter nav (only search-tap / scrubber populate `uiState.scrollToOffset`). Saved-position restore is otherwise one-shot in `makeUIView` ŌĆö not re-run when only the text changes.
3. So when Chapter 2's text is applied, the `UITextView` keeps Chapter 1's bottom `contentOffset.y` (Ōēł `maxOffset`). The user sees the END of Chapter 2, not its start.
4. Worse: that stale near-`maxOffset` offset re-satisfies `sendScrollPosition`'s bottom-boundary predicate (`offset >= maxOffset - boundarySlack`, `TXTTextViewBridgeCoordinator.swift:392-401`) on the next settle ŌåÆ `didScrollPastBottomBoundary()` fires again ŌåÆ `goToNextChapter()` again ŌåÆ **cascading multi-chapter skip**. `isChapterNavInFlight` only serializes overlapping loads; it does not stop the next *settled* scroll from re-triggering.

**RE-SCOPED 2026-05-16 (user directive)**: The discrete chapter-SWAP approach is rejected outright ŌĆö not patched. The user wants TXT scroll mode to **scroll continuously, smoothly, and endlessly across chapter boundaries** with no jump at all. The boundary-detect-then-swap design (PR #681) is the wrong model for this bug. Per the user's tracking decision, the fix stays under bug #180 (not split into a separate feature) and **chapter awareness must be preserved** ŌĆö TOC jumps, per-chapter reading progress, and feature #48's chapter-scoped highlight pipeline all continue to work under continuous scroll.

**Fix direction (re-scoped)**:
1. **Abandon the boundary-swap.** Remove / disable `didScrollPastBottomBoundary` / `didScrollPastTopBoundary` driving `goToNextChapter()` / `goToPreviousChapter()` as the scroll-mode chapter-advance mechanism. (Chrome-button chapter nav can remain.)
2. **Render chaptered TXT as one continuous scrollable surface in Scroll layout.** The app already has whole-document continuous renderers ŌĆö flat-mode `UITextView` and the chunked `UITableView` (`TXTChunkedReaderBridge`, used for >500K UTF-16). The fix routes chaptered TXT in Scroll layout through a continuous renderer so scrolling never stops at a chapter edge. Scrolling must stay **smooth** ŌĆö no relayout hitch, no content jump when crossing a boundary (the chunked renderer's windowing already handles large books; reuse it rather than swapping `UITextView` text).
3. **Preserve chapter awareness over the continuous surface.** Maintain a chapter-offset index (each chapter's global UTF-16 start) so: (a) TOC tap jumps to the right scroll offset; (b) per-chapter progress + the scrubber compute correctly from the continuous offset; (c) feature #48's chapter-scoped highlight pipeline still maps globalŌåöchapter-local offsets. `currentChapterIdx` becomes a *derived* value from scroll position, not a render-mode switch.
4. **Memory**: the chunked `UITableView` path already lazy-renders rows for huge books; continuous cross-chapter scroll should build on that windowing, not load every chapter's full attributed string at once.

**Scope note**: this is feature-sized work carried on a bug row by explicit user choice (2026-05-16) ŌĆö it skips the `/feature-workflow` gates, but the fix still warrants a written plan (Understand ŌåÆ design the continuous-scroll architecture ŌåÆ RED ŌåÆ GREEN ŌåÆ REFACTOR ŌåÆ Verify) given the architecture surface. Cross-ref: bug #165 (EPUB has the same discrete-vs-continuous question); feature #48 (chapter-scoped highlight pipeline that must keep working); feature #60 (reader chrome ŌĆö the design bundle is paginated, so any *new* scroll-mode chrome/toggle UI is undesigned and falls under rule 51 ŌåÆ file `Design needed:` if a new surface is required; behavior-only continuous scroll reusing existing chrome does not).

**Note**: the summary-table row was never flipped from `TODO` to `FIXED` after PR #681 merged ŌĆö a separate tracker-hygiene slip; the row is set to `REOPENED` here. GH: #614 (REOPENED)

### Bug #179 ŌĆö TXT reading content obscured by Dynamic Island on restore + chapter-nav (FIXED 2026-05-15)

**Original symptom (FIXED in v3.21.31, commit 306e54f)**: First-open at offset 0 ŌĆö DI obscured first line. Resolved via `safeAreaTopInset` threaded through `TXTTextViewBridge` / `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` and applied to `textContainerInset.top`.

**REOPENED 2026-05-14**: User reports the symptom recurs on two paths the original fix did not cover:
1. **Reopening the TXT file** (saved reading position > 0) ŌĆö first visible line lands behind DI.
2. **Navigating to a new chapter** (chapter-mode or scroll-mode jump) ŌĆö chapter start lands behind DI.

**Repro (REOPENED scenario A ŌĆö restore)**: Open any TXT book ŌåÆ scroll to mid-chapter (saved position offset > 0) ŌåÆ close book ŌåÆ reopen book. **Pre-fix**: the restored character lands at the visible top of the scrollView, behind the DI. **Post-fix (v3.21.62)**: restored chapter renders cleanly below DI; reopen of mid-chapter saved position lands the header at yŌēł200pt (below the ~110pt DI cutoff).

**Repro (REOPENED scenario B ŌĆö chapter nav)**: Open any TXT book with detected chapters ŌåÆ tap "Next chapter" button or scrubber-jump to a new chapter. **Pre-fix**: chapter start clipped behind DI. **Post-fix (v3.21.62)**: chapter-nav renders new chapter header at yŌēł200pt (below DI) across multiple chapter transitions.

**Root cause analysis history**:
- The REOPEN row body proposed that `attemptScrollRestore` was missing a `textContainerInset.top` subtraction. The previous bugfix-cron iteration (2026-05-15 earlier) tried this fix and Codex thread `019e2743` rejected it as mathematically wrong: `contentOffset.y = lineY` IS correct when `textContainerInset.top` includes the safe-area inset; the proposed subtract/add would land the glyph at visible y=0 instead of `textContainerInset.top` (below DI).
- The TRUE root cause is upstream of the scroll math. The container view wraps its content in `GeometryReader { proxy in TXTTextViewBridge(safeAreaTopInset: proxy.safeAreaInsets.top, ...) }`. The parent `ReaderContainerView` applies `.ignoresSafeArea(edges: .top)` (chrome-overlay layout) and bug #73 documented (in `ReaderChromeBar.swift:85`) that `GeometryReader` returns `0` from `proxy.safeAreaInsets.top` momentarily on initial render and across rebuild gaps. On the bridge's first `makeUIView`, `textContainerInset.top = base(16) + 0 = 16` ŌĆö and `contentOffset.y = lineY` (or default 0) lands the glyph at visible y = 16, BEHIND the DI. By the time SwiftUI's later layout pass reaches `updateUIView` with the measured ~59pt, the 0.15s-delayed `attemptScrollRestore` has already fired against the under-insetted textView. Same race fires on chapter-nav rebuild (`chapterAttrString = nil` swaps to `loadingView` then back, creating a fresh `TXTTextViewBridge` whose first `makeUIView` hits the same un-measured `proxy.safeAreaInsets.top`).

**Fix (v3.21.62)**: new `ReaderSafeAreaResolver` static helper that reads the device's actual top safe-area from `UIWindow.safeAreaInsets.top` (the bug #73 escape pattern from `ReaderChromeBar.windowSafeAreaTop`, but with broader activation-state coverage and a `lastKnownNonZeroTop` cache). The resolver's logic is active-first (foreground active scene's max top inset wins, even when 0 ŌĆö covers landscape iPad / Stage Manager), inactive-as-warmup (foreground inactive scenes consulted only when no active scene exists; an inactive 0 falls through to cache rather than fabricating a zero state), then cache. Every TXT/MD container view's bridge entry point now passes `ReaderSafeAreaResolver.topInsetWithFallback(proxy.safeAreaInsets.top)` instead of `proxy.safeAreaInsets.top` directly ŌĆö guaranteeing the bridge sees a correct ~59pt even before SwiftUI has measured.

The scroll math (`attemptScrollRestore`, `scrollToMatchedOffset`) is unchanged ŌĆö Codex round 1 of `019e2743` correctly verified it. The bug was upstream, in the inset feed.

**Codex audit `019e2893` (3 rounds, ship-as-is)**: round 1 found 2 Mediums (activation-state too narrow + multi-window scene mis-selection); round 2 found 1 Medium (active-pass-zero shouldn't fall through to inactive in landscape); round 3 clean. Test gate: 908 Swift Testing pass including new 10-case `ReaderSafeAreaResolverCombineSuite` covering both-zero, geom-only, window-only, both-equal, geom-larger, window-larger, negative clamps, iPad-landscape baseline. Pre-FIXED simulator verify on iPhone 17 Pro Sim at v3.21.62: opened `war-and-peace.txt`, navigated chapter 1ŌåÆ2 (tap Next), confirmed chapter 2 header at yŌēł200pt (below ~110pt DI); tapped Back, retapped book, confirmed saved-position reopen lands chapter 2 header below DI; tapped Next again to chapter 3/4, confirmed chapter 3 header also below DI. Evidence: `dev-docs/verification/artifacts/bug-179-postfix-chapter-2-reopen-below-di-20260515.png` + `dev-docs/verification/artifacts/bug-179-postfix-chapter-nav-below-di-20260515.png`. Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-611-txt-di-overlap-restore-and-chapter-nav-audit.md`. Follow-up: a SwiftUI/UIView/window-seam regression harness for restore + chapter-nav under nonzero safe area is recommended but not yet built ŌĆö vreader's test layer doesn't currently have such a harness; pure-function `combine(_:_:)` coverage is the test floor, device verification is the test ceiling. GH: #611

**Note**: MD scroll mode shares `TXTTextViewBridge` ŌĆö same regression likely. Native paged MD path (`NativeTextPagedView`) was explicitly OUT OF SCOPE in the original fix; reassess in the re-fix. GH: #611 (REOPENED)

### Bug #178 ŌĆö MD native mode Chinese conversion silently no-ops ŌĆö picker enabled but SimpTradTransform never applied (REPORTED 2026-05-14)

**Repro**: Open any MD file with Simplified Chinese content ŌåÆ Settings ŌåÆ Chinese Text ŌåÆ Traditional. Picker accepts the change (not disabled) ŌåÆ content renders unchanged ŌĆö conversion is silently skipped.
**Root cause** (`MDReaderContainerView.swift`, `MDReaderViewModel.swift`): neither file reads `settingsStore.chineseConversion` nor calls `TextMapper.apply(transforms:to:)`. Feature #28 WI-A only wired TXT native mode. `ReaderSettingsPanel.chineseConversionDisableReason` (line 513) explicitly enables the picker for MD (`fmt == .txt || fmt == .md`) ŌĆö making the setting appear functional when it is not.
**Contrast**: `TXTReaderContainerView` wires `SimpTradTransform` at 8 call sites across chapter, flat, and chunked render paths.
**Fix**: mirror TXT's pattern ŌĆö read `settingsStore?.chineseConversion` in `MDReaderContainerView`, include it in the rebuild key (alongside `fontSize`, `fontName`, etc.), and call `TextMapper.apply(transforms:to:)` on the parsed Markdown source text.
**Discovered**: 2026-05-14 via gpt-5.5 code review of issue #493 design decision. GH: #606

### Bug #176 ŌĆö AZW3/MOBI TTS silently fails ŌĆö speaker button + `vreader-debug://tts?action=start` both no-op (Foliate-rendered formats have no text-extraction case in `loadBookTextContent`)

**Repro**: Open any AZW3/MOBI book ŌåÆ tap the speaker button in the reader chrome OR fire `vreader-debug://tts?action=start`. Reproduced 2026-05-13 on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.5) at v3.21.17 (commit `a0ec073`) with bundled `mini-azw3.azw3` (Project Gutenberg #1064, "The Masque of the Red Death").
**Observed**: No TTS control bar appears. `vreader-debug://snapshot` after the start URL shows `ttsState: "idle"`, `ttsOffsetUTF16: null` ŌĆö the production `TTSService.state` never transitioned from `.idle`. No error toast, no spinner, no log entry ŌĆö silent failure. Screenshot evidence: `dev-docs/verification/artifacts/feature-26-r3-02-azw3-tts-start-20260513.png`.
**Expected**: TTS starts speaking the AZW3 text. `ttsState` transitions to `"speaking"`. TTS control bar (ŌÅĖ/ŌŚŠ/1.2x) appears at the bottom of the reader. Same behaviour as TXT/MD/PDF/EPUB.
**Root cause** (code-read confirmed at `vreader/Views/Reader/ReaderAICoordinator.swift`'s `loadBookTextContent(fileURL:format:)`): the `switch format` statement has cases for `"txt"` / `"md"`, `"pdf"`, and `"epub"`, but **no case for `"azw3"` or `"mobi"`**. Falls through to `default: return nil`. Result: `loadedTextContent` stays nil. `startTTS()` in `ReaderContainerView+Sheets.swift:17` guards both call sites with `if let text = ai.loadedTextContent, !text.isEmpty { ... }` ŌĆö both fail when the format isn't TXT/MD/PDF/EPUB, so `ttsService.startSpeaking(...)` is never called.
**Why this is a bug not a feature**: `FormatCapabilities.azw3` declares `.tts` capability (`FormatCapabilities.swift`), so the speaker button IS shown in the reader chrome ŌĆö the capability is advertised. `FoliateTTSAdapter` (`vreader/Services/Foliate/FoliateTTSAdapter.swift`) exists with `startTTSJS()`/`nextTTSJS()`/`initTTSJS(granularity:)` ŌĆö the JS-side adapter is already shipped. The wire-up between the capability-advertised button and the available Foliate adapter is missing. Implementation exists but is unwired for AZW3/MOBI ŌĆö classic bug, not a never-implemented feature.
**Two fix paths** (do NOT pick one ŌĆö fix-cron will diagnose):
- (a) Add an `"azw3"` / `"mobi"` case to `loadBookTextContent` that extracts text from the Foliate webview (e.g., via `webView.evaluateJavaScript("document.body.innerText")` or a `readerAPI` helper). Keeps the unified AVSpeechSynthesizer pipeline ŌĆö same TTS service, same sentence highlighting (feature #40) wired through `currentOffsetUTF16`.
- (b) Branch `startTTS()` on format: for Foliate formats, evaluate `FoliateTTSAdapter.initTTSJS(granularity:) + startTTSJS()` in the webview instead of going through `ttsService.startSpeaking`. Foliate's in-webview TTS pipeline (foliate-js's own TTS) handles the speech ŌĆö but then the AVSpeechSynthesizer code path + sentence-highlight feature #40 don't apply to AZW3.
**Filed by verify cron 2026-05-13** during feature #26 round-3 verification of the deferred Foliate slice. Same gap likely affects MOBI (same Foliate render path). EPUB is unaffected because `loadBookTextContent` has an explicit `"epub"` case using `EPUBParser` + `EPUBTextExtractor.stripHTML`.

### Bug #177 ŌĆö Library grid cards in the same row sit at different vertical positions (REPORTED 2026-05-13)

**Repro**: Open the Library with Ōēź2 books in the same grid row where one has an author label or reading-time label and another doesn't. The cover images' top edges are visibly at different Y positions.
**Root cause** (`BookCardView.swift:38,46`): author and reading time are conditionally included in the `VStack`, so card total height varies. `LazyVGrid` determines row height from the tallest card, then **vertically centers** shorter cards within that height. Cards with more metadata (author + reading time) appear highest; cards with no metadata appear lowest.
**Fix**: add `Spacer(minLength: 0)` as the last child of `BookCardView`'s `VStack` (line ~57, before `.frame(maxWidth: .infinity, alignment: .leading)`). All cells then fill the full row height, centering is a no-op, and all cover tops align at the same Y.
**Note**: Not related to cover images ŌĆö `CoverContainerView` already uses a fixed 2:3 `aspectRatio` so cover heights are uniform. The misalignment is purely from the variable-height metadata below the cover.

### Bug #174 ŌĆö AI provider row tap does nothing for editing (REPORTED 2026-05-13)

**Repro**: Settings ŌåÆ AI Providers (1+ profile saved) ŌåÆ tap any provider row.
**Observed**: Active indicator updates (radio button fills), but no edit sheet appears. The only edit path is a leading-edge swipe gesture (`swipeActions(edge: .leading)`), which is non-standard and not surfaced by any affordance on the row.
**Expected**: Tapping a row opens the edit form, OR a visible pencil/edit affordance indicates how to edit.
**Root cause 1 ŌĆö UX discoverability** (`AIProviderListView.swift:127-128`): The row `Button` action is wired exclusively to `viewModel.setActive(profile.id)`. Edit lives only behind `.swipeActions(edge: .leading)` at lines 175-184. No pencil icon, no Edit button in the toolbar, no tap-to-edit path.
**Root cause 2 ŌĆö potential SwiftUI sheet state race** (`AIProviderListView.swift:64-66`): `.sheet(isPresented: $showEditor)` captures `editingProfile` at evaluation time. The swipe button sets `editingProfile = profile` and `showEditor = true` synchronously; if SwiftUI evaluates the sheet closure before committing `editingProfile`, the sheet opens with `existing: nil` (add-new mode instead of edit mode). Fix: migrate to `.sheet(item: $editableItem)` where `editableItem` is either a `ProviderProfile` (edit) or a sentinel (add-new).
**Fix direction**: (a) Make row tap open edit form ŌĆö change the `profileRow` button action to open the editor; move `setActive` to a trailing-edge swipe or a dedicated "Set Active" label; OR (b) Add a pencil button next to each row label; either way, also migrate to `.sheet(item:)` to eliminate the state-race risk.

### Bug #175 ŌĆö TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests suite crashes/hangs on `highlights from ch0 are dropped when rendering ch2`, blocking full vreaderTests run

**Repro**: `DEVELOPER_DIR=/Applications/Xcode.app/Contents/Developer xcodebuild test -project vreader.xcodeproj -scheme vreader -destination 'platform=iOS Simulator,name=iPhone 17 Pro' -only-testing:vreaderTests/TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests` on clean `main` (commit be51d7d). Confirmed pre-existing: reproduces with WI-4c-c branch stashed.
**Symptom**: Swift Testing reports `ŌŚć Test "highlights from ch0 are dropped when rendering ch2" started.` followed by `Restarting after unexpected exit, crash, or test timeout`. Test harness re-launches but cannot recover; subsequent test suites (AutoPageTurnerTests, TTSServiceSpeedControlTests) listed as failing but never actually executed ŌĆö they're collateral from the crash. Suite is at `vreaderTests/Views/Reader/TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests.swift` (feature #48 WI-1, commit 540722b).
**Why this is a bug not a feature**: `TXTReaderContainerView.chapterLocalHighlightRanges` was implemented and shipped (feature #48 WI-1 merged). The test exists in the repo and is in the default test plan ŌĆö it's expected to run. It runs the first test (`chapterModeKeepsRangesWithinChapter`) cleanly per other suites' precedent, but crashes specifically on the ch0-vs-ch2 case. The implementation is in place; the test or the implementation has a latent crash bug surfaced by this scenario.
**Impact**: blocks `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests` from completing cleanly. Workaround: exclude `TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests` with `-skip-testing` until root cause is fixed. Test-gate evidence for unrelated WIs (e.g., WI-4c-c) requires running with the skip flag.
**Possible root causes** (none yet investigated): (1) `chapterLocalHighlightRanges` returns an NSRange whose location/length overflow when the ch0ŌåÆch2 mapping puts the result out-of-bounds for the chapter text; (2) test fixture's chapter offsets create a pathological case the production code doesn't guard against; (3) Swift Testing `@Test` actor-isolation interaction with the helper.
**Fix scope** (deferred ŌĆö this row files; fix-cron picks up): read `TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests.swift` lines around the named test (line 73 per grep), trace the inputs into `TXTReaderContainerView.chapterLocalHighlightRanges`, isolate the crash with a minimal repro, fix.
**Filed by feature cron 2026-05-13** during feature #45 WI-4c-c Gate 3 test gate.

### Bug #163 ŌĆö EPUB reading content obscured by Dynamic Island at chapter start (REOPENED)

**Repro**: Open any EPUB ŌåÆ navigate to chapter start ŌåÆ first 1ŌĆō2 lines of text clipped behind the Dynamic Island.
**Prior fix (PR #513, 2026-05-11)**: `EPUBWebViewBridge` reads `safeAreaInsets.top` via `GeometryReader`, injects it into `UIScrollView.contentInset.top` + `verticalScrollIndicatorInsets.top`, and subtracts it from paged column height. Passed unit tests + simulator verify but user reports regression on device.
**Re-investigation needed**: Confirm safe-area value is non-zero at the time of injection; check whether `GeometryReader` proxy gives the correct inset when the chrome bar is visible vs hidden; check if `updateUIView` change-detection path fires correctly; check if the fix covers the case where the reader first opens (vs inset changes after load). Also check if the `contentInsetAdjustmentBehavior = .never` override is fighting the manual inset on iOS 17+.

### Bug #172 ŌĆö Haptic feedback on bookmark-add missing in TXT, EPUB, PDF, and AZW3/MOBI readers (only MD fires)

**Repro**: Open any TXT / EPUB / PDF / AZW3 book ŌåÆ tap the bookmark toolbar icon ŌåÆ bookmark is added successfully BUT no haptic vibration on the device.
**Expected** (feature #7): UIImpactFeedbackGenerator(.light) fires on every successful bookmark add across all formats. Feature #7 row at `docs/features.md` describes WI-002: "UIImpactFeedbackGenerator(.light). 5 tests."
**Observed**: Haptic fires only when adding a bookmark in the Markdown reader. The other four formats add the bookmark silently.
**Root cause** (code-confirmed):
- `MDReaderContainerView.swift:245` wires `hapticFeedback: HapticFeedbackProvider()` into `ReaderNotificationDeps`, and the bookmark-add path runs through `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleBookmarkRequest` (which calls `deps.hapticFeedback?.triggerLightImpact()` at line 88).
- `TXTReaderContainerView.makeNotificationDeps()` (line 402-434) constructs `ReaderNotificationDeps` WITHOUT the `hapticFeedback` parameter ŌĆö defaults to `nil`. Even though the TXT bookmark-add flows through the same `handleBookmarkRequest`, the optional-chained call is a no-op.
- `EPUBReaderContainerView.swift:166-177`, `PDFReaderContainerView.swift:218-area`, and `FoliateReaderContainerView.swift:80-area` do NOT use `ReaderNotificationHandlers` at all ŌĆö they handle `.readerBookmarkRequested` inline with their own `.onReceive` blocks that call `persistence.addBookmark(...)` directly, bypassing the haptic dispatch entirely.
**Fix direction**: Either (a) make `TXTReaderContainerView.makeNotificationDeps()` pass `hapticFeedback: HapticFeedbackProvider()` (one-line change mirroring MD line 245) AND migrate EPUB/PDF/Foliate to route their `.readerBookmarkRequested` observers through `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleBookmarkRequest` (deps-based pattern); OR (b) extract a small `BookmarkHaptic.fire()` helper and call it inline in each reader's bookmark observer alongside `persistence.addBookmark`. Option (a) is cleaner long-term but touches 4 files; option (b) is a 4-line change in 4 places.
**Why this is a bug, not a feature**: feature #7 is `DONE`; the `BookmarkFeedback` 5-test suite covers `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleBookmarkRequest` with a `MockHapticProvider`. The test surface proves the dispatch works through the handler; the container-level wiring per format is what's missing. So the implementation exists but is wired to only 1 of 5 reader paths ŌĆö classic bug.
**Filed by verify cron 2026-05-12** during feature #7 round-2 verification (haptics are sim-unobservable, but the wiring gap surfaced via code-read of the dispatch path).

### Bug #171 ŌĆö EPUB paged mode shows two-column layout instead of single-page flip

**Repro**: Open any EPUB ŌåÆ AA ŌåÆ EPUB Layout ŌåÆ Paged ŌåÆ observe content on iPhone 17 Pro.
**Observed**: Two columns of text appear side-by-side. Navigation advances the scroll by one viewport width but both columns remain visible simultaneously, making the layout look like a split newspaper view rather than page-flip reading.
**Root cause** (code-confirmed): `EPUBPaginationHelper.paginationCSS(viewportWidth:viewportHeight:)` (`EPUBPaginationHelper.swift:31`) sets `column-width: (viewportWidth - 40)px` with no `column-count` constraint. CSS `column-width` is a hint (minimum desired column width); the browser will create as many columns as fit. On iPhone 17 Pro the viewport / book CSS combination allows two columns to render simultaneously.
**Expected**: One full-width page of content at a time; tap/swipe advances to the next page ŌĆö matching Kindle / Apple Books paged navigation convention.
**Fix direction**: Add `column-count: auto` is not enough ŌĆö need to ensure one column per page. Options: (a) set `column-width: {viewportWidth}px` (full viewport width per column, no gap) so only one column fits; (b) add `max-height: {viewportHeight}px; overflow: hidden` on body and use a fixed-size column wrapper. Must preserve horizontal `scrollLeft` navigation math in `navigateToPageJS`.

### Bug #170 ŌĆö OPDS catalog detail view renders blank after NavigationLink tap; no spinner, no entries, no error

**Repro**: Library ŌåÆ globe (OPDS Catalogs) ŌåÆ + (Add Catalog) ŌåÆ Name="Gutenberg", URL="https://www.gutenberg.org/ebooks.opds/" ŌåÆ Save ŌåÆ tap the saved row.
**Observed**: a sheet pushes onto the NavigationStack showing only a back chevron at top-left. NO `ProgressView("Loading catalog...")`, no `navigationTitle`, no `feedContent` entries, no `errorState` Retry button. Captured at t+0.5s, t+2.5s, t+10.5s, t+17s ŌĆö all identical-blank. AX dump in the detail-view area returns only the back button + an empty AXGroup; no AXStaticText, no AXProgressIndicator.
**Why this matters**: per `OPDSBrowserView.body` (`vreader/Views/OPDS/OPDSBrowserView.swift:39-48`), the Group { } branches on `isLoading && feed == nil` (ŌåÆ ProgressView), `errorMessage` (ŌåÆ errorState), `feed` (ŌåÆ feedContent). The blank-with-back-chevron-only state means `isLoading == false && feed == nil && errorMessage == nil` ŌĆö i.e. **`.task` never set isLoading=true at all**, OR set it and then reset to false without populating feed/errorMessage. Either way, `loadFeed` did not run to completion or never started.
**Root cause hypothesis (NOT confirmed ŌĆö fix scope)**: the `.task { await loadFeed(url: catalogURL) }` modifier on `OPDSBrowserView` (line 52) is nested inside `OPDSCatalogListView`'s NavigationLink destination (`OPDSCatalogListView.swift:96-104`), inside the `NavigationStack` wrapping `OPDSCatalogListView` (`LibraryView.swift:276`), inside the `.sheet(isPresented: $isShowingOPDSCatalogs)` (`LibraryView.swift:275`). Known SwiftUI iOS 26 issue: `.task` can be skipped or cancelled instantly when a destination view is presented via NavigationLink inside a NavigationStack inside a sheet. Suspect surface includes: (a) `.task` lifecycle in this nested presentation; (b) URL validity check in the NavigationLink wrapper (`URL(string: catalog.url)` is non-nil for `https://www.gutenberg.org/ebooks.opds/` ŌĆö confirmed via repl); (c) `OPDSClient.fetchFeed` silently throwing a cancellation. **Possible fix directions**: replace `.task` with `.onAppear { Task { await loadFeed(...) } }`; OR seed `isLoading = true` as the initial @State value so the spinner shows immediately on view appear regardless of when loadFeed actually runs; OR move the fetch trigger to `init()` or to a `.task(id: catalogURL)` variant.
**Reproducible 100%** on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.149 (commit de37ad4) with the bundled Gutenberg endpoint. Curl probe from the host confirms `https://www.gutenberg.org/ebooks.opds/` returns 200 with valid Atom/OPDS XML ŌĆö backend works.
**Filed by verify cron 2026-05-11T20:50** during feature #36 round-4 verification of the per-catalog navigation deferred leg. 11 screenshot artifacts under `dev-docs/verification/artifacts/feature-36-r4-*-20260511.png`.
**Cross-ref**: feature #36 row already documents "per-catalog navigation" as deferred ŌĆö this bug formalizes the deferral and identifies the suspected lifecycle root cause. Feature #36 cannot flip to VERIFIED until this is fixed.

### Bug #168 ŌĆö EPUB font family setting has no effect ŌĆö fontFamily never injected into CSS

**Repro**: Open any EPUB ŌåÆ AA ŌåÆ Font Family ŌåÆ switch to Serif or Monospace ŌåÆ text rendering unchanged.
**Root cause** (code-confirmed): `ReaderTheme.epubOverrideCSS` signature (`ReaderTheme.swift:75`) has parameters `(fontSize:lineHeight:letterSpacing:)` ŌĆö no `fontFamily` parameter. The call site in `EPUBReaderContainerView.swift:313` passes only `fontSize`, `lineSpacing`, and `letterSpacing`; `typography.fontFamily` is never forwarded. By contrast, TXT correctly consumes `fontFamily` via `TXTViewConfig.fontName` (line 612 of `ReaderSettingsPanel.swift`). The setting is persisted and tracked ŌĆö the EPUB CSS injection path is simply unwired.
**Fix direction**: (1) add `fontFamily: ReaderFontFamily = .system` to `epubOverrideCSS`; (2) emit CSS `font-family` stack (`.system` ŌåÆ `-apple-system, system-ui, sans-serif`; `.serif` ŌåÆ `Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif`; `.monospace` ŌåÆ `'SF Mono', Menlo, 'Courier New', monospace`); (3) update call site. CJK characters fall back to system CJK font automatically ŌĆö expected behavior for an English typeface picker.

### Bug #167 ŌĆö EPUB overscroll bounce reveals white background instead of theme color

**Repro**: Open any EPUB in Sepia or Dark theme ŌåÆ drag content up past the very top (or down past the bottom) until the scroll view rubber-bands ŌåÆ white strip appears in the overscroll area.
**Root cause** (code-confirmed): `EPUBWebViewBridge.swift:163` sets `webView.scrollView.backgroundColor = .clear`. The CSS injection (`ReaderTheme.epubOverrideCSS`) correctly paints `html, body { background-color: <theme> }` inside the document, but when iOS bounces the scroll view past content bounds it exposes the scroll view's own background, which is transparent and falls through to the host UIView/UIWindow (white by default). Result: white bleed on overscroll for every non-Light theme.
**Expected**: overscroll area matches the current theme background color (Sepia Ōēł `rgb(245,237,217)`, Dark Ōēł `rgb(28,28,31)`).
**Fix direction**: set `webView.scrollView.backgroundColor = store.theme.backgroundColor` in `makeUIView` (and update in `updateUIView` when `themeCSS` changes). `ReaderTheme.backgroundColor: UIColor` already exists for all three themes ŌĆö this is a one-liner fix. Cross-format: AZW3/MOBI (`FoliateViewBridge`) also uses WKWebView and may share the same gap.

### Bug #166 ŌĆö Font size visually inconsistent across formats; slider max too small for EPUB

**Repro**: Set font size to any value (e.g. 20pt) ŌåÆ open same book content in TXT, then EPUB, then PDF ŌåÆ text appears at noticeably different visual sizes despite the same numeric setting. Also: drag font size slider to maximum (32pt) in EPUB ŌåÆ text still appears small.
**Root cause**: Each format pipes font size through a different rendering system with no perceptual normalization layer. TXT/MD use UITextView native pt (1:1 screen points); EPUB injects CSS `font-size` via WKWebView where the book's own stylesheet compounds or conflicts; PDF uses PDFView's own scaling; AZW3/MOBI goes through Foliate-js with its own CSS defaults. Bug #57 (FIXED) addressed EPUB-vs-TXT mismatch at one specific point; the broader cross-format normalization gap was never addressed, and the slider ceiling of 32pt was insufficient for EPUB where CSS rendering makes pt-values appear smaller than UIKit equivalents.
**Expected**: Same numeric font-size value produces perceptually consistent text size across all supported formats; slider maximum is large enough that EPUB text at max setting is comfortably readable.
**Fix direction**: (a) **DONE in this iteration** ŌĆö `TypographySettings.fontSizeRange` raised from `12...32` to `12...64`; slider auto-extends because it uses the constant directly. (b) **OPEN** ŌĆö Audit per-format CSS/font injection to apply a calibration factor so the same pt value renders at consistent perceived size across formats. This is feature-class scope (per-renderer measurement + unified ptŌåÆlogical-size mapping); should be split out as a separate feature row or follow-up bug when planned. Reported by user 2026-05-10. GH: #491

### Bug #165 ŌĆö EPUB chapter navigation unintuitive: no side-tap, scroll-within vs button-between mismatch (FIXED 2026-05-21)

**Repro**: Open a multi-chapter EPUB ŌåÆ scroll to end of chapter ŌåÆ must tap explicit "Previous | Next" button to cross chapter; tapping sides of screen only toggles chrome. No consistent swipe/tap navigation across chapters.
**Impact**: Every EPUB user. Cross-chapter navigation requires a dedicated button tap that breaks reading flow; no side-tap to flip chapter is the opposite of every major e-reader convention (Kindle, Moon+, etc.).
**Fix direction**: (a) Remove "Previous | Next chapter" buttons; let scroll flow continuously between chapters. (b) Wire side-tap into native EPUB renderer to dispatch prevChapter/nextChapter (proper fix for bug #162's deferred "option (b)"). Cross-ref: bug #162 (tap zones no-op in native EPUB); feature #25 (tap zones ŌĆö native mode deferred).

**FIXED v3.38.36** ŌĆö implemented design `dev-docs/designs/vreader-fidelity-v1/project/design-notes/reader-navigation.md` ┬¦2.2 (paged-mode chapter wrap). New pure helper `EPUBChapterNavigationRouter` decides, given (currentPage, totalPages, currentSpineIndex, spineCount), whether a side-tap should turn within the chapter, wrap forward to chapter N+1's first page, wrap backward to chapter N-1's last page, or bounce at start/end of book. New one-shot `EPUBChapterWrapPendingTarget` (@MainActor reference type) carries the "land on last page" intent across the async chapter load ŌåÆ `onPaginationReady` boundary. Container wiring in `EPUBReaderContainerView+ChapterWrap.swift` consumes the router decision; `EPUBReaderContainerView` and `EPUBReaderContainerView+Navigation.swift` cancel any pending wrap intent at every non-wrap chapter navigation site (TOC / search / annotation jump, scrubber seek) via a dedicated `cancelBecauseUnrelatedNavigationStarted()` entry point ŌĆö addresses a Codex round-1 High finding that the intent would otherwise bleed into unrelated chapter loads. Router's `0..<spineCount` guards collapse stale spine indices to safe bounces (round-1 Medium). Codex audit thread `019e47c8 ŌåÆ 019e47cd`, 2 rounds, verdict `follow-up-recommended` (round-2 Medium accepted: container call-site coverage is by helper-contract tests only because driving the SwiftUI container in XCTest requires a `ModelContainer` boot; dedicated entry-point naming provides grep precision). 29 new unit tests (18 router + 11 pending-target). Device-verified on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.5) via `vreader-debug://eval` driving `webkit.messageHandlers.contentTapHandler.postMessage({x, w})`: forward wrap from ch1 ŌåÆ ch2, backward wrap from ch2 ŌåÆ ch1, bounce at start (left-tap from ch1 stays), bounce at end (right-tap from ch2 stays); evidence `dev-docs/verification/bug-165-20260521.md` + screenshots `dev-docs/verification/artifacts/bug-165-verify-*.png`. **Scope deferral**: design ┬¦2.3 (continuous cross-chapter scroll mode ŌĆö chapters rendered in one scrollable column with hairline divider + skeleton-pulse + lazy ┬▒1 chapter load) is a multi-chapter WKWebView document architecture; filed as a follow-up feature to ship separately. ┬¦2.2 bounce visual affordance ("subtle horizontal nudge") deferred until the design specifies the animation curve. Full suite 6986 tests pass under `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests -parallel-testing-enabled NO`. GH: #489

### Bug #164 ŌĆö TTS starts reading from article beginning instead of current scroll position

**Repro**: Open any book, scroll to middle, activate TTS ŌåÆ speech starts from the very beginning of the article, not from the currently visible content.
**Impact**: Every TTS user who starts playback mid-document must listen through already-read content or manually skip, defeating the use case.
**Fix direction**: Pass the current `currentOffsetUTF16` / locator as the start offset when initiating TTS playback, instead of defaulting to offset 0.

## Summary

| #  | Summary                                                                                               | File/Area  | Severity | Status   | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| -- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------- | -------- | -------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| 282| TXT TOC takes ~1.3s to scroll to the current chapter ŌĆö the `TOCSheet` Contents `.task(id:)` retry loop slept before EVERY scroll (`[100, 300, 600]` ms) with no immediate t=0 jump, so the authoritative scroll fired at cumulative ~1000ms, each animated 0.3s ŌåÆ settle ~1.3s; on long TOCs only the last (slowest) attempt landed because earlier ones targeted not-yet-materialized `LazyVStack` rows | Reader/TOC | Low | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-29** (branch `fix/bug-282-txt-toc-scroll-timing`). **Root cause**: the Bug #248 scroll-restore retry loop (`TOCSheet.swift` `.task(id: currentChapterScrollTarget)`) slept `[100, 300, 600]` ms *before* each `proxy.scrollTo`, so the first scroll didn't even fire until 100ms and the authoritative one not until ~1000ms; each was animated 0.3s, so the list visibly crept to the chapter over ~1.3s. **Fix**: extracted the schedule to the pure `TOCSheet.scrollRetryDelaysMilliseconds = [0, 80, 240]` and rewrote the loop to sleep only the *incremental* gap between cumulative delays ŌĆö the first attempt (cumulative 0) fires immediately and **unanimated**, so a materialized row lands the instant the sheet appears; later attempts stay a short animated fallback (0.25s) for the long-TOC not-yet-materialized case. No layout/design change (rule 51 ŌĆö restores designed instant-scroll behavior); the nested outer-`ScrollView`/`ScrollViewReader` structure is unchanged (the t=0 jump lands deterministically once the row exists, so the redundant nesting need not be restructured). **Test** (REDŌåÆGREEN): `TOCSheetTests` ŌĆö `scrollRetryScheduleLeadsImmediate` (first delay == 0) + `scrollRetryScheduleMonotonicAndFast` (Ōēź2 attempts, non-decreasing, last Ōēż 500ms). Cross-ref #248 (the fix this regressed). GH: #1259 |
| 279| EPUB page content can be freely pinch-zoomed and dragged off-axis instead of being locked to clean vertical scroll / discrete page-turns | vreader/Views/Reader/EPUBWebViewBridge.swift, vreader/Views/Reader/EPUBWebViewBridgeJS.swift | Medium | FIXED | **RE-FIXED 2026-05-31 (v3.41.5)** ŌĆö #1269 locked the OUTER WKWebView scrollView but the DEFAULT continuous-scroll path scrolls the INNER DOM `#vreader-scroll-root`, which was unconstrained. Unlike the Foliate spike (`FoliateSpikeView`, viewport `maximum-scale=1, user-scalable=no`) and the continuous-scroll bootstrap (`EPUBContinuousScrollJS.bootstrapDocumentHTML`, `maximum-scale=1`) which bake the pin into their own constructed HTML, the legacy single-chapter path loads the EPUB's own XHTML (head not authored by us), so nothing constrained pinch-zoom or off-axis drag. **Fix** (two seams, defense in depth): (1) `applyScrollLock(to:)` pins the scroll view ŌĆö `minimumZoomScale=1`, `maximumZoomScale=1`, `bouncesZoom=false`, `isDirectionalLockEnabled=true` (pins pan to one axis), `alwaysBounceHorizontal=false`; called in `makeUIView`. (2) `viewportLockJS` ŌĆö a static IIFE injected as a `.atDocumentEnd` WKUserScript that upserts a `width=device-width, initial-scale=1, maximum-scale=1, user-scalable=no` viewport meta into each loaded chapter. Idempotent; harmless in continuous mode (overwrites the bootstrap meta with a stricter equivalent); paged-mode `scrollLeft` navigation unaffected (`isScrollEnabled=false`). Pure-code, no new visible chrome (rule 51 ŌĆö constrains existing content gestures only). **Test** (REDŌåÆGREEN): `EPUBWebViewBridgeTests` ŌĆö `EPUBWebViewBridgeScrollLockTests` (zoom/bounce/directional-lock/idempotency against a real `UIScrollView`), `EPUBWebViewBridgeViewportLockJSTests` (JS shape + injection-safety), `EPUBWebViewBridgeViewportLockDOMTests` (live-`WKWebView` DOM harness: upsert-when-absent / overwrite-permissive-in-place / head-less). Full suite 7598 tests green. **Audit**: Codex Gate-4 thread `019e745e-1d10-73c0-8397-9bdabdb3d940`, 2 rounds, final verdict ship-as-is (`.claude/codex-audits/fix-bug-279-epub-viewport-lock-audit.md`). | 266| Bilingual translation is misaligned ŌĆö a paragraph's translation is injected under the WRONG paragraph (reported on EPUB: the first paragraph's translation lands at the third paragraph's position). The render-side enumerate and the translation-side segmentation are matched by blind positional index with no enforced 1:1 contract | Reader/Bilingual | High | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-26** (branch `fix/issue-1152-bilingual-translation-misaligned`, v3.39.14) ŌĆö EPUB enumerate now counts LEAF blocks only (`querySelector` skips block-in-block), + shared `BilingualPairing` 1:1 count-safety (mismatch ŌåÆ source-only) in both EPUB+Foliate pipelines. Never a wrong pairing. 49 bilingual tests + full suite green; Codex Gate-4 thread `019e60ca` 1 round follow-up-recommended. Residual unit-model divergence (`<pre>`/mixed-content) + Foliate-host enumerate leaf-fix tracked as Bug #268/#1159. **Ō£ģ VERIFIED via close-gate exception 2026-05-26** (`dev-docs/verification/bug-266-20260526.md`): the never-wrong-pairing guarantee is structurally proven by `EPUBBilingualPipelineTests` + `FoliateBilingualPipelineTests` (count-mismatch ŌåÆ source-only, both renderers); device-level alignment verification is CU-free-blocked (AI path + #268 fixture). GH #1152 closed. **Filed 2026-05-25 (user triage ŌĆö "EPUB translation misalignment. The translation of the first paragraph was inserted into the position of the third paragraph. Other book formats may have similar issues as well.")** **Root cause (code-read, high confidence)**: feature #56 bilingual pairs translations to paragraphs by BLIND POSITIONAL INDEX, zipping two segmentations produced by independent code on different representations. (1) **Render enumerate** ŌĆö `EPUBBilingualJS.bilingualEnumerateJS` walks `document.body.getElementsByTagName('*')` keeping `BLOCK_TAGS={p,li,blockquote,pre,dd,dt}` in DOM order; because it walks ALL descendants, nested block tags **double-count** (a `blockquote`/`li`/`dd` containing a `p` enumerates BOTH the container and the child). (2) **Translation segments** ŌĆö `ChapterTranslationService` (`ChapterTranslationService.swift:123`) uses `ChapterSegmenter.paragraphs(in: sourceText)` on the EXTRACTED PLAIN TEXT, which does NOT double-count nesting. (3) **The zip** ŌĆö `EPUBBilingualPipeline.translationsByBid`: `for i in 0..<min(blocks,segments): map[blocks[i].bid]=segments[i]` ŌĆö trusts `blocks[i] ŌēĪ segments[i]`. When the enumerate yields extra/missing blocks vs the text segmenter (nested `blockquote>p`/`li>p`, `<pre>` with blank lines, list grouping, plain-text-extraction divergence), every pairing past the first divergence drifts; a leading epigraph / 2-item structure the DOM splits into 2 extra blocks but the segmenter merges = the reported para-1ŌåÆpara-3 (+2) drift. **No enforced 1:1 contract** ŌĆö the `BLOCK_TAGS` set excludes headings with a comment that it "keeps enumerate/segment counts aligned" (a hand-tuned approximation, defeated by nesting); the only count check (`ChapterTranslationService.swift:133` `sourceParagraphCount==segments.count`) compares the segmenter to ITSELF for cache-staleness, never against the enumerate count. `BilingualBlock.text` is carried "for debugging only", not used to anchor the match. **Cross-format (user hypothesis CONFIRMED by code-read)**: shared architectural flaw ŌĆö every format feeds the same `ChapterSegmenter` segments into its own render enumerate via the same index-zip: EPUB (`EPUBBilingualPipeline`), AZW3/MOBI (`FoliateSpikeView` bilingual), TXT (`TXTReaderContainerView+Bilingual`), MD (`MDReaderContainerView+Bilingual`). The fix should fix the contract once, not the EPUB tag set. **Fix direction**: anchor instead of trusting position ŌĆö either translate the enumerated blocks' own `text[]` (the enumerate becomes the single segmentation source ŌåÆ 1:1 by construction), or match segmentsŌåöblocks by normalized-text equality, or at minimum enumerate only LEAF block elements + assert `blocks.count==segments.count` and fall back to source-only on mismatch (show no translation, never a wrong one). Apply uniformly across all 5 formats; regression test with a chapter containing nested `blockquote>p` / lists / `<pre>`. **Severity High** ŌĆö systematic correctness defect in a shipped feature; any chapter with nested block structure misaligns, and a wrong translation under a paragraph is MISLEADING (worse than absent). Downgrade to Medium only if bilingual is treated as niche/opt-in. See Open Bug Details. GH: #1152 |
| 265| AZW3/MOBI reading position is neither saved nor restored on the live Foliate reader ŌĆö closing and reopening a book always resumes at the very beginning, losing the reader's place. | 264| DebugBridge `search` driver stalls forever when a stale persistent-FTS metadata row survives `reset` ŌĆö `setup()`'s `alreadyIndexed` branch never marks the book in-memory-indexed when `getSegmentBaseOffsets` is nil, so `isIndexed()` stays false and the search-result-tap path can't be driven CU-free | DevTools/Verification | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-26** (branch `fix/issue-1141-search-fts-stale-row`, v3.39.20). Two-part fix: (1) **product** ŌĆö `ReaderSearchCoordinator.setup()`'s persisted-index branch is now a 4-way split keyed on the new pure `formatRequiresSegmentOffsets(_:)` (txt/md only): TXT/MD with offsets ŌåÆ restore; persisted+already-in-memory ŌåÆ no-op; **TXT/MD persisted but offsets nil = STALE ŌåÆ `removeBook` + re-index** (breaks the silent no-op); EPUB/PDF persisted + offsets nil = NORMAL ŌåÆ new `SearchService.markPersistentlyIndexed` marks `indexedKeys` in memory WITHOUT re-indexing (the FTS content already exists), so `isIndexed()` is honest and the driver's index-wait completes ŌĆö and EPUB/PDF no longer wastefully re-index on every reopen. (2) **harness** ŌĆö `vreader-debug://reset` now calls `ReaderSearchCoordinator.wipeSearchIndex(...)` to delete the persistent FTS store dir for a true clean slate. **Codex Gate-4** thread `019e6351`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is: round-1 caught a High (the original format-agnostic re-index would have re-indexed every EPUB/PDF reopen) ŌĆö fixed via the format dimension. Tests: `formatRequiresSegmentOffsets` table + `markPersistentlyIndexed` behavior + augmented store precondition (`indexBook` ŌåÆ `isBookIndexed && offsets==nil`); 64 tests across 3 suites green. `setup()`-level integration testing needs a store-injection seam (follow-up, Codex-accepted). Audit log `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-1141-search-fts-stale-row-audit.md`. **Filed 2026-05-22 by the Feature #2 / GH #400 round-6 verify run** (`dev-docs/verification/feature-2-20260522-round6.md`). **Symptom**: `vreader-debug://search?query=<q>&index=<n>` (Bug #238 driver) opens the search sheet but the query field stays empty, no results render, no result is tapped, no navigation happens ŌĆö on BOTH the fast-indexing `war-and-peace` TXT fixture and the `mini-epub3` EPUB fixture. Live debug-log stream shows `search observer: received query=ŌĆ” index=ŌĆ”` ŌåÆ `search: posted notification` ŌåÆ **30s later** `search observer: timed out waiting for search index`, with ZERO `Search`/`EPUBTextExtractor`/`indexBook` activity. The 30s wait is `ReaderContainerView+DebugBridgeSearch.swift:109` `awaitSearchIndexed(timeout: 30.0)` polling `service.isIndexed(fingerprint:)`, which never flips. **Root cause (code-read + SQLite inspection, high confidence)**: `vreader-debug://reset` (`RealDebugBridgeContext.reset()`) deletes only the SwiftData library books ŌĆö it does NOT clear the **separate** persistent FTS store at `Library/Application Support/SearchIndex/search.sqlite3`. So after `reset` + `seed`, the seeded book's fingerprint is STILL present in `search_metadata` from a prior session (confirmed: `war-and-peace` `txt:bd8285ŌĆ”:1705` + `mini-epub3` `epub:f284fdŌĆ”:2198` rows both present, with an EMPTY `segment_base_offsets` column). `ReaderSearchCoordinator.setup()` (`ReaderSearchCoordinator.swift:70`) calls `store.isBookIndexed(fingerprintKey:)`, which returns `true` iff a `search_metadata` row exists (`SearchIndexStore.swift:253` ŌĆö `SELECT 1 ŌĆ” LIMIT 1`, content-blind) ŌåÆ `alreadyIndexed = true` ŌåÆ takes the restore branch (line 89) ŌåÆ `getSegmentBaseOffsets(...)` returns `nil` because the column is empty ŌåÆ the `if let offsets` guard fails ŌåÆ `service.restoreSegmentOffsets(...)` (the ONLY call that does `service.indexedKeys.insert(key)` on that branch) **never runs** ŌåÆ `service.isIndexed()` returns `false` forever ŌåÆ the driver's 30s index-wait times out ŌåÆ query never set, result never tapped. **Confirmed by repair**: deleting `SearchIndex/` then re-seeding ŌåÆ the second indexed `search?query=ŌĆ”&index=0` fire builds the index, persists offsets (`length(segment_base_offsets)`=72 for war-and-peace), taps the result (`tapping result 0 ŌåÆ ŌĆ”segment:7:118`), and navigates (`navigateToChapter: idx=3`). With that workaround the full Feature #2 highlight lifecycle then verifies on both formats (round-6 PASS). **Impact**: blocks ALL CU-free search-result-tap verification (Feature #2 / GH #400; Bug #182 / GH #621's own close-gate DOM-probe; any future search-tap repro) whenever a stale `search_metadata` row with empty/nil offsets is left behind by `reset`. **Real-user exposure (narrower but real)**: the `alreadyIndexed && getSegmentBaseOffsets==nil ŌåÆ neither re-index nor in-memory-mark` gap in `setup()` could also bite a real user whose persistent index row exists but lacks restorable offsets (e.g. an index row written by an older build with a different offset schema, or an interrupted prior index that committed the metadata row before offsets) ŌĆö search would silently return 0 hits until a force-reindex. **Fix direction** (either or both): (1) **harness** ŌĆö have `vreader-debug://reset` also wipe the persistent FTS store (delete `SearchIndex/search.sqlite3` or call `store.removeBook(fingerprintKey:)` for each removed book) so reset is a true clean slate; (2) **product robustness** ŌĆö in `setup()`'s `alreadyIndexed` branch, when `getSegmentBaseOffsets` returns nil (or the FTS content rows are absent), treat the book as NOT indexed and fall through to `enqueueBookIndexing` instead of silently skipping; or unconditionally mark `indexedKeys` for a present-metadata row even when offsets are nil (TXT/MD need offsets for locator math, so re-index is the safer choice). Add a regression test: a `search_metadata` row with nil `segment_base_offsets` ŌåÆ `setup()` re-indexes (don't leave `isIndexed()` false). **Severity Medium** ŌĆö primary impact is DEBUG/verification-only (no Release/user UI for `reset`), same class as Bug #238/#253/#255/#259/#263 (verification-tooling gaps); the secondary real-user edge (stale-schema FTS row) is a latent correctness risk worth the `setup()` hardening. Verification-only finding ŌĆö filed, not fixed (verify cron files bugs, never fixes them). GH: #1141 |

| 261| AZW3/MOBI reader renders body text too large ŌĆö Foliate font-size pipeline (calibrator `foliate: 1.12` multiplier, or em-compounding against the book's own CSS) overshoots the perceived size of TXT/EPUB at the same slider value | Reader/AZW3 | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-22** in `fix/issue-1131-azw3-font-size-overshoot` (v3.39.6). **Root cause = candidate 2 (em-compounding), NOT the multiplier.** Device-measured (CU-free DebugBridge `eval` of `getComputedStyle` inside the Foliate content document, unified 28): EPUB body 31.4px / `<p>` 31.4px (flat); AZW3 body 31px (so `foliate: 1.12` is CORRECT ŌĆö matches EPUB, candidate 1 ruled out) but `<p>` COMPOUNDED to 35.65px (book `p{1.15em}`) ŌåÆ 43.4px (book `.big{1.4em}`), +15% to +40%. The overshoot was the book's own `em`/`%` descendant CSS multiplying against the injected `body` base, because `FoliateStyleMapper` pinned ONLY `body` font-size and lacked the cascade-flatten rule EPUB already has (`ReaderThemeV2+EPUBCSS`). **Fix** (CSS-injection-only, mirrors EPUB): `FoliateStyleMapper.themeCSS` now pins `html, body` (not body alone, so `rem` resolves against the calibrated size ŌĆö AZW3 `html` was stuck at the 16px UA default), adds the text-container reset `p,div,span,ŌĆ”,section,article,aside,main,header,footer,figure{font-size:inherit !important; line-height:inherit !important}` (widened beyond EPUB's list for Kindle KFX semantic-container immunity), and `h1-h6{font-size:revert !important}`. `color` deliberately omitted (Foliate doesn't theme colors). **Feature #70 NOT regressed** ŌĆö `FontSizeCalibration.standard.foliate = 1.12` + `FontSizeCalibrator` untouched; the fix is purely the Foliate CSS. REDŌåÆGREEN `FoliateStyleMapperCascadeFlattenTests` (6 tests). Codex audit thread `019e4c36` verdict `follow-up-recommended` (0 must-fix code defects; Medium = a `!important`-in-book residual that EPUB shares, accepted; Low = brittle injection test, made structural). Test gate: 7071/7071 unit tests TEST SUCCEEDED. Pre-FIXED verify on iPhone 17 Pro Max Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.39.5 build: post-fix realistic Kindle CSS (em/%, no `!important`) flattens ALL elements to 31px = body, matching EPUB; AZW3 `html` now 31px; evidence `dev-docs/verification/bug-261-20260522.md` + artifact `bug-261-fix-verify-azw3-flat-31px-20260522.png`. **Residual (accepted, shared w/ EPUB)**: a book using `!important` on its own font-size can still win at equal precedence + later source order ŌĆö same boundary EPUB has, not a #70 regression; real Kindle CSS rarely uses `!important`. Original triage below. **Filed 2026-05-21 (user triage ŌĆö "the fontsize is too big")**. **Symptom**: AZW3/MOBI body text renders perceptibly larger than TXT / EPUB at the same font-size slider value (and too large at the default). **Font sizing IS implemented for AZW3** ŌĆö `FoliateSpikeView.themeCSS(for:)` routes `store.typography.fontSize` (default 18) through `FontSizeCalibrator.calibratedFoliateSize(forUnified:)` ŌåÆ `FoliateStyleMapper.themeCSS(fontSize:ŌĆ”)` ŌåÆ Foliate-js `setStyles`. So this is a too-large *output*, not a missing pipe ŌåÆ bug, not feature. **Two candidate root causes**: (1) **calibration mis-tune** ŌĆö the `.standard` profile sets `foliate: 1.12` (`FontSizeCalibration.swift:88`, same as `epub: 1.12`), but the source comment flags these as *"conservative, identity-leaning estimates"* whose literals *"Gate-5 behavioral verification confirms or re-tunes"* ŌĆö and feature #491's calibration was never device-verified for the Foliate target specifically. If Foliate-js renders px larger than the EPUB WKWebView at the same value, 1.12 is too high for AZW3. (2) **em-compounding** ŌĆö Foliate-js applies the user font-size as a base on a root element; AZW3/MOBI (Kindle) books frequently carry their own `em`/`%`-based font-size CSS, which multiplies against the injected base (bug #166's root-cause note already documented *"the book's own stylesheet compounds or conflicts"* for WebView formats). The calibrator assumes the px maps ~directly, so a book with `body{font-size:1.2em} p{font-size:1.1em}` renders ~32% larger than the slider implies. **Fix direction**: (a) device-measure AZW3 cap-height at unified 24 on iPhone 17 Pro Sim vs the TXT anchor and re-tune the `foliate` multiplier (cheap, no architecture change ŌĆö the literal is explicitly designed to be re-tuned); (b) if em-compounding is the dominant cause, normalize the book's root font-size in the injected CSS (e.g. force `html{font-size:<px>}` + neutralize book `body`/`p` em-bases) so the slider value maps predictably. Measure first (a) before reaching for (b). **Cross-ref Bug #260** ŌĆö the Display button that hosts the font-size slider lives in the bottom chrome, which is currently NOT mounted for AZW3 (#260), so an AZW3 user cannot even reach the slider to work around this. The two bugs compound; #260 should land first so #261 is adjustable. Cross-ref Bug #166 (FIXED ŌĆö cross-format inconsistency, residual calibration split to feature #491). **Severity Medium** ŌĆö text is readable, just oversized; adjustable once #260 restores the Display affordance. See Open Bug Details. GH: #1131 |

| 259| Incremental rebuild silently drops the injected `vreader-debug` URL scheme ŌĆö the inject build-phase declares no output files, so Xcode skips it on incremental builds, shipping an Info.plist without the scheme; `simctl openurl` then fails (error 115) until a clean build | DevTools/Verification | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-26** (branch `fix/issue-1128-incremental-debugbridge-inject`, v3.39.21). Root cause was DEEPER than the filed diagnosis ŌĆö device verification revealed two compounding causes: (1) the inject postCompile phase had `inputFiles` but no `outputFiles`, so Xcode skipped it when `DebugBridge.plist` was unchanged; (2) **dominant** ŌĆö on incremental builds Xcode re-ran `ProcessInfoPlistFile` AFTER the inject script (order inject ŌåÆ ProcessInfoPlistFile ŌåÆ CodeSign), CLOBBERING the injection. Fix: `basedOnDependencyAnalysis: false` (always-run) + declare the BUILT Info.plist (`$(TARGET_BUILD_DIR)/$(INFOPLIST_PATH)`) as an `inputFiles` entry so XCBuild schedules inject AFTER ProcessInfoPlistFile (inputs avoid the duplicate-output failure that outputs cause). **Device-verified CU-free on iPhone 17 Pro Sim**: clean build ŌåÆ openurl reset exit 0; touch a Swift file ŌåÆ INCREMENTAL build (order now ProcessInfoPlistFile ŌåÆ Injected) ŌåÆ openurl reset exit 0 + `vreader-debug` scheme present in installed Info.plist (pre-fix the incremental openurl failed error 115). Codex Gate-4 thread `019e6363`, 1 round, ship-as-is. Config-only (rule-10 TDD-exempt); audit log `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-1128-incremental-debugbridge-inject-audit.md`. **Filed 2026-05-21 by the Bug #258 / GH #1125 `/fix-issue` run** (discovered during the auto-page-turn fix's DebugBridge verification). **Symptom**: after an incremental `xcodebuild build`, `xcrun simctl openurl <UDID> vreader-debug://...` fails with error 115 (scheme not registered in the installed binary's Info.plist); a clean build restores it. **Root cause**: the build phase that injects the `vreader-debug` URL scheme into Info.plist has NO declared output files, so Xcode's incremental dependency analysis skips re-running it ŌåÆ incremental rebuild ships an Info.plist WITHOUT the scheme. **Impact**: verification-harness reliability ŌĆö likely explains intermittent DebugBridge failures in prior verify-cron iterations ("no active reader" / empty seed-log / `open` no-op when driving `vreader-debug://` against an incrementally-built install). **Fix direction**: declare the inject build-phase's output files (the generated Info.plist or a sentinel) in `project.yml` so incremental analysis re-runs it, OR mark the phase always-out-of-date; regenerate pbxproj; confirm via incremental rebuild ŌåÆ `simctl openurl vreader-debug://reset` succeeds without a clean build. **Workaround until fixed**: verify/bugfix crons do a clean build (or fresh `-derivedDataPath`) before driving DebugBridge. **Severity Medium** ŌĆö DEBUG-only/harness reliability (no Release/user impact) but silently undermines every CU-free verification run. | 258| Auto page turning is inert in MD paged mode ŌĆö `AutoPageTurner` advances the navigator (`nav.nextPage()`) on its timer, but that advance never syncs to the observable `uiState.pagedCurrentPage` that drives both the view render and `snapshot.position` | Reader/MD | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-21 by the Feature #31 / GH #381 round-9 verify run** (`dev-docs/verification/feature-31-20260521-round9.md`, `result: partial`). **Symptom**: at v3.39.1 (main `aedcee23`), with the round-8 blockers Bug #215 (MD paged layout, FIXED PR #1100) + Bug #239 (paged side-tap producer, FIXED PR #1098) BOTH resolved, MD paged mode now engages cleanly (seeded `--seed-md-multi-page` book paginates to 6 pages, indicator "Page 1 of 6", content renders cleanly above the chrome) ŌĆö but auto page turning does NOT advance. CU-free repro on iPhone 17 Pro Sim: `defaults write com.vreader.app readerEPUBLayout paged` + `readerAutoPageTurn true` + `readerAutoPageTurnInterval 2.0`, `launch --uitesting --seed-md-multi-page --reader-default-layout=paged`, open `md:00ŌĆ”c0c002:9231` via `vreader-debug://open`, then `vreader-debug://snapshot` over time. **Expected**: `snapshot.position` increases as pages auto-advance every 2s. **Observed**: `position` stays `"0"` across 20s (10├Ś interval, no gesture); a clean re-run with 16s fully untouched (no intervening DebugBridge calls) also stays `"0"`, screenshot still "Page 1 of 6". **Root cause** (code-read): `AutoPageTurner.scheduleTimer` (`vreader/Services/AutoPageTurner.swift:130`) advances by calling `navigator.nextPage()` directly on `NativeTextPageNavigator` (mutating internal `base.currentPage`); it does NOT post `.readerNextPage` nor call `syncPagedState()`. But `NativeTextPagedView` renders from the explicit `currentPage: uiState.pagedCurrentPage` param (`MDReaderContainerView.swift:394`; `NativeTextPagedView.swift:34-35` ŌĆö *"Explicit page index so SwiftUI detects page changes and triggers updateUIView"*), and `uiState.pagedCurrentPage` is copied from `nav.currentPage` ONLY in `TextReaderUIState.syncPagedState()` (`TextReaderUIState.swift:78-85`), called ONLY from the `.readerNextPage`/`.readerPreviousPage` observers (`MDReaderContainerView.swift:247-262`) + `updatePaginationIfNeeded` ŌĆö paths auto-turn bypasses. So the timer mutates navigator state the view does not observe: (1) the view never re-renders (`updateUIView` not triggered); (2) `viewModel.totalProgression` never updates ŌåÆ `.readerPositionDidChange` never posts ŌåÆ `snapshot.position` stays flat. **Why unit tests pass while live fails**: `AutoPageTurnerTests` use a `MockNavigator` asserting `nextPageCallCount`/`currentPage` on the mock ŌĆö they prove the timer FIRES `nextPage()`, but never exercise the `NativeTextPagedView`/`pagedCurrentPage` view-sync. **Scope**: MD paged mode is the only affected surface that matters ŌĆö `FormatCapabilities.autoPageTurn` is `.md`-only (TXT lost it via bug #157's gate + has no `NativeTextPagedView` branch; EPUB/PDF/AZW3 never had `AutoPageTurner` wiring per bug #156), so this gap IS the entire Feature #31 criterion-5 failure. **Distinct from**: bug #156 (which formats wire AutoPageTurner ŌĆö FIXED), bug #157 (TXT chapter-path bypass ŌĆö FIXED), bug #191 (AutoPageTurner recursion crash ŌĆö FIXED), bug #215 (MD paged layout engaging ŌĆö FIXED), bug #239 (side-tap producer ŌĆö FIXED). Finally root-causes the "deferred live-advancement" thread running since Feature #31 round-1 (2026-05-07). **Fix direction** (NOT implemented ŌĆö verification-only finding): (a) have `AutoPageTurner` post `.readerNextPage` so it routes through the observer that calls `syncPagedState()`; or (b) have the containers observe the navigator's page and re-sync `pagedCurrentPage` + position each tick. Add a regression test that drives a timer-driven advance through the container's observable state (not via MockNavigator alone). **Severity Medium** ŌĆö the auto-page-turn feature is end-to-end non-functional, but it's an opt-in convenience (default OFF), MD-only, and has no data/correctness impact. Blocks Feature #31's `VERIFIED` flip. **FIXED 2026-05-21** in `fix/issue-1125-autopageturn-paged-sync` (v3.39.2): chose fix-shape (b) NOT (a) ŌĆö direction (a) [timer posts `.readerNextPage`] is FATAL because that observer also calls `autoPageTurner?.pause()` (Bug #131's manual-turn-pauses-auto-turn), which would halt auto-advance after one tick. Instead added `AutoPageTurner.onAdvance: (@MainActor () -> Void)?` fired after each timer-driven `nextPage()`; `TextReaderUIState.updateAutoPageTurner` installs it to run `syncPagedState()` + a container-supplied `onAutoAdvancePersist` (ŌåÆ `viewModel.updateScrollPosition`) ŌĆö the SAME sync the `.readerNextPage` observer does, MINUS the `pause()`. Regression tests: `AutoPageTurnerTests.timerAdvance_invokesOnAdvanceCallback` (the timerŌåÆview-sync bridge the MockNavigator suite missed) + `timerAtLastPage_doesNotInvokeOnAdvance` + `stop_preventsFurtherOnAdvance`; MockNavigator now fires the delegate on advance. Codex audit `ship-as-is` (1 round, 0 functional findings). CU-free verify on iPhone 17 Pro Sim: `snapshot.position` climbs `1085ŌåÆ3523ŌåÆ4758ŌåÆ7258ŌåÆ8440` over 12s untouched then auto-stops at last page (pre-fix `0/0/0/0`); screenshot "Page 6 of 6" (pre-fix stuck "Page 1 of 6"). Evidence: `dev-docs/verification/bug-258-20260521.md`. MD verified live; TXT wired symmetrically (defensive ŌĆö `FormatCapabilities.autoPageTurn` is MD-only). Verify-cron filed; fixed by fix-issue. GH: #1125 |
