| 247| WebDAV restore loses book titles ŌĆö restored TXT/MD/PDF books show `restore_<sha256>` filename as title instead of the original book name | Backup/Restore | High | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-21** (branch `fix/issue-1075-webdav-restore-book-titles`, v3.38.31). **Filed 2026-05-20 (user triage ŌĆö "the books from web-dav backups lost there names")**. **Symptom (user-confirmed)**: after restoring from WebDAV backup, books in the library show titles like `restore_abc123ŌĆ”` (the content-addressed temp filename) instead of the original book name. User confirms TXT is affected; suspects EPUB/AZW3/PDF may share the bug. **Root cause (code-read, high confidence)**: `BookFileMaterializer.materializeOneDownload` (`vreader/Services/Backup/BookFileMaterializer.swift:194-196`) writes the downloaded blob to a temp file named `restore_<sha256>.<originalExtension>` and then hands it to `BookImporter.importFile(at: tempURL, source: .restore)`. `BookImporter` derives the book title from `MetadataExtractor.extractMetadata(from: fileURL)`. For formats with no embedded title metadata ŌĆö **TXT** (`TXTMetadataExtractor` uses filename) and **MD** (`MDMetadataExtractor`, same) ŌĆö the title becomes the SHA-prefixed temp name. For formats with optional embedded titles (**PDF** in particular), when the PDF metadata is empty the fallback is the same filename-derived path ŌåÆ also broken. **EPUB** (`EPUBMetadataExtractor` reads `<dc:title>` from `package.opf`) and **AZW3** (reads MOBI header title) usually escape this bug because their formats embed titles in the file contents. **The manifest already carries the correct title** in `BackupLibraryEntry.title: String?` (see `BackupSectionDTOs.swift:262`), but `BookFileMaterializer` doesn't pass it to the importer, and `BookImporter` has no `titleOverride` parameter ŌĆö so the manifest title is unused at materialize time. Latent since feature #46 (WebDAV materializing restore, VERIFIED) and feature #47 (selective restore, VERIFIED) shipped. **Fix direction (3 viable options)**: (a) **easiest** ŌĆö in `BookFileMaterializer` write the temp file with the manifest's title-derived filename (e.g. `<title>.<originalExtension>`, sanitised + uniquified with the SHA suffix); (b) **more correct** ŌĆö add a `titleOverride: String?` parameter to `BookImporter.importFile(...)` and pass `entry.title` from the materializer (preserves the manifest as the source of truth); (c) **post-import patch** ŌĆö after `importFile` returns, update the persisted Book's `title` if it equals the temp-file filename AND the manifest carries a non-nil title. Option (b) is the cleanest and matches the manifest-as-source-of-truth invariant the plan already documents. **Severity High** ŌĆö every restore on a non-embedded-title format loses every book's name, making the restored library unusable without manual rename. Includes feature #46 + #47 device-verified-VERIFIED scope. See Open Bug Details. GH: #1074 |

| 242| XCUITest runner sandbox blocks `xcrun simctl openurl` ŌĆö host-side bridge driving is the only working path for DebugBridge commands from inside the test binary | Tests/DebugBridge | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-20 by the bug #240 (`/fix-issue` GH #1049) run** as "Bug #240b" inside row 240's notes; promoted to its own row here. **Repro**: inside an XCUITest binary (e.g. `VerificationDebugBridgeHelper.openURL(...)`), invoke `xcrun simctl openurl booted vreader-debug://...`. The call exits 72 with stderr `Failed to load CoreSimulatorService ŌĆö running with a sandbox profile` (NSPOSIXErrorDomain 61 "Connection refused"). The XCUITest runner sandbox does not have a path to the host's `CoreSimulatorService` XPC endpoint, so the URL never reaches the running app under test. The bridge URL handlers themselves work perfectly when invoked from outside the runner sandbox (e.g. the verify cron's host-side bash drivers); they cannot be reached from inside the test binary. **Impact**: The DebugBridge commands shipped 2026-05-20 (#976 `vreader-debug://search`, #986 TXT/MD `vreader-debug://highlight`, #845 EPUB `vreader-debug://highlight`) drive correctly via host-side scripts but not from `VerificationDebugBridgeHelper.openURL(...)` inside the test process. **Fix direction**: directions (1) + (3) per the GH body ŌĆö (1) document the host-vs-runner split explicitly so future agents stop assuming the in-runner path works, and (3) accept the `XCTSkipUnless(bridgeReachable())` pattern PR #1053 introduced as the official in-runner workaround; bridge-driven verification flows go through host-side scripts. **Severity Medium** ŌĆö the runner-side bridge driving genuinely can't work, but workarounds exist (`XCTSkipUnless` in-runner + host-driven scripts), so it's a documentation gap rather than a missing capability. **FIXED 2026-05-20** (this PR, branch `fix/issue-1054-debugbridge-xcuitest-sandbox-docs`): `docs/subsystems/debug-bridge.md` gained a "Driving the bridge from a verification flow" section that names the HOST-driven path (the primary, working path used by every verify cron driver under `dev-docs/verification/*`), the in-runner path via `VerificationDebugBridgeHelper.openURL(...)` (NSPOSIX 61 ŌĆö does NOT work, sandbox blocks the XPC connection), and the `XCTSkipUnless(bridgeReachable())` pattern PR #1053 introduced; `docs/architecture.md` gained a one-line cross-reference so the constraint surfaces at the architecture level. Multiple agents' early Bash calls inadvertently run from `/Users/ll/workspace/vreader` (orchestrator's main checkout) instead of the spawned worktree. When the agent later runs `xcodegen generate` for a version bump while stray files lie in main's working tree, those stray files get added to `vreader.xcodeproj/project.pbxproj` as references ŌĆö producing a build that fails on any clean clone ("file not found in compile sources"). **Session evidence**: (1) WI-7bŌåÆWI-8 transition produced stray `ReaderMoreMenuBilingualTests.swift` references in `project.pbxproj` without the source file being git-tracked ŌåÆ required hotfix PR #1029 (v3.37.19) to restore main; (2) bugfix #957 agent explicitly self-reported "my first 4 Bash calls accidentally cd'd into /Users/ll/workspace/vreader (main checkout) instead of staying in the worktree, so the initial REDŌåÆGREEN cycle ran in the main repo. I patched this mid-flow by saving the diff to /tmp, reverting the main checkout, and re-applying the patch inside the worktree on the proper branch before committing" ŌĆö caught by the agent itself, no main contamination shipped. **Root cause hypothesis**: `Agent` tool's worktree-isolation mode creates the worktree but doesn't `cd` the spawned process into it ŌĆö the agent's Bash tool starts with cwd = the orchestrator's cwd; the agent must explicitly `cd "$WORKTREE"` in every Bash call (the tool persists cwd between calls, but a single early call from the wrong cwd writes files to the wrong place). **Fix directions (pick one)**: (1) harness-side: `Agent(isolation: worktree)` should set the spawned subprocess's initial cwd to the worktree path; (2) brief template: codify "cd \"$WORKTREE\" first" guard in a default preamble for every worktree-isolated agent (this is the workaround currently in use ŌĆö the briefs from WI-10 onward include this discipline and subsequent agents haven't repeated the contamination); (3) runtime guard: pre-tool-use hook on `Bash` that detects cwd != worktree for a worktree-isolated session and auto-corrects or errors. **Severity Medium** ŌĆö produces broken main when it bites (proven this session: hotfix #1029 cost an extra PR), and remains latent if multiple agents in the same session repeat the pattern without the explicit cd-first discipline in the brief. GH: #1050 |
| 235| AZW3/MOBI reader ŌĆö scroll mode does not scroll continuously across chapter (section) boundaries | Reader/AZW3 | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-19 (user triage, re GH #614 / bug #180 ŌĆö "so are the epub and azw3")** ŌĆö the AZW3/MOBI reader has the same cross-chapter scroll discontinuity bug #180 fixed for TXT. AZW3/MOBI renders via Foliate-js, which navigates section-by-section (`prevSection` / `nextSection`); scroll mode (bug #189, FIXED) scrolls *within* a section but a chapter boundary is a discrete `nextSection()` swap, not a continuous scroll. Implemented-but-discontinuous ŌåÆ bug, consistent with #180 (TXT) / #165 (EPUB). EPUB cross-chapter scroll is already bug #165 (open); AZW3 had no tracking ŌĆö neither #165 (EPUB-only) nor `reader-navigation.md` (scopes EPUB/MD) covers it. See Open Bug Details. **FIXED 2026-05-20** (worktree branch `worktree-agent-a71ccad431f39e678`): added a `#maybeCrossSectionBoundary()` private method to the Foliate paginator (`vreader/Services/Foliate/JS/paginator.js`) and wired it into the IMMEDIATE (non-debounced) `#container` scroll listener so cross-chapter advance happens during the live fling (not 250ms after it stops). The helper short-circuits unless `scrolled && !#locked && #view && (atEnd \|\| atStart)` with edge math `atEnd = viewSize - end <= 2` (matches `#scrollNext`'s epsilon) and `atStart = start <= 0` (matches `#scrollPrev`'s threshold); when atEnd it calls `#turnPage(1)` and when atStart `#turnPage(-1)`, reusing the same #locked-protected machinery that programmatic `next()` / `prev()` use. The debounced 250ms listener still owns relocate/anchor maintenance unchanged. Bundle (`foliate-bundle.js`) rebuilt via the new pinned local esbuild (`package.json` + `package-lock.json`, esbuild 0.28.0; `build-bundle.sh` now uses `./node_modules/.bin/esbuild` via `npm ci` bootstrap + node>=18 preflight ŌĆö closes the previous `npx esbuild` cross-machine non-determinism). Regression guard: new `FoliatePaginatorScrollBoundaryTests` Swift Testing suite (15 tests, all passing) pins helper presence in both files, IMMEDIATE-listener wiring (scan window bounded by the next `.addEventListener(` call to distinguish from the debounced listener), exact epsilon literals, direction-specific `#turnPage(┬▒1)` calls, scrolled-mode accessors, and `#adjacentIndex(┬▒1)` in both directions ŌĆö fires if the helper is removed, the wiring collapses back to debounced-only, the epsilons drift, or paginator.js diverges from the built bundle. Codex audit `019e4407`, 3 rounds, ship-as-is (R1: debounce-too-late Medium + epsilon-asymmetry Low + test-quality Medium + esbuild-pin Low; R2: stale-comment Low + esbuild-still-advisory Low; R3: npm-install-vs-ci Low + node-engines-not-declared Low ŌĆö all 8 findings resolved). | 228| `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests` shares the `DebugReaderRegistry.shared` singleton ŌĆö same parallel-test isolation defect class as bug #227, on the `awaitReader`/`waiters` path | DevTools/* | Medium | FIXED | **Numbering note (2026-05-19)**: this row keeps 228. GH #938 and GH #939 were filed concurrently by two different agents and BOTH titled themselves "Bug #228", colliding two rows in this file. Resolved per the #225/#226 collision precedent ŌĆö this row (GH #939, the `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests` singleton-isolation bug, currently being fixed by a `/fix-issue` run) keeps 228; the separate AZW3/MOBI Foliate overlay-strip row (GH #938) was renumbered to the next free number 229. The GH #939 issue title still reads "Bug #228" ŌĆö `docs/bugs.md` is the source of truth and now says 228. **Filed 2026-05-19 by the bug #227 (`/fix-issue` GH #932) run** ŌĆö surfaced by the Codex implementation audit. `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests.makeRegistry()` does `DebugReaderRegistry.shared.reset()` and returns `.shared`. Swift Testing runs `@Test` methods in parallel; the suite's tests install `Waiter`s via `awaitReader` and suspend, and `DebugReaderRegistry.reset()` resumes every pending `waiters` entry with `.awaitReaderTimeout` ŌĆö so a *concurrent* test's `shared.reset()` can resolve another test's suspended `awaitReader` waiter with a spurious timeout. **Same defect class as bug #227** but on a different store (`waiters`, not `settleWaiters`) and a different method (`awaitReader`, not `awaitReaderSettled`). Bug #227's fix isolated the three **settle** suites (`DebugReaderRegistrySettle{Core,EdgeCase,Cleanup}Tests`) to fresh per-test `DebugReaderRegistry.makeIsolatedForTests()` instances; `AwaitReaderTests` was left out of #227's scope because it is **not currently observed failing** ŌĆö a latent flake risk, not an active failure ŌĆö and was filed separately per the working agreement (discover-a-bug ŌåÆ file, don't fix in an unrelated PR). **Fix direction**: mirror the #227 fix ŌĆö switch `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests.makeRegistry()` to `DebugReaderRegistry.makeIsolatedForTests()` so each test gets its own isolated registry; a fresh instance starts empty so the `reset()` call becomes unnecessary. Optionally also isolate `RealDebugBridgeContextTests` and the XCTest `DebugReaderRegistryTests` (lower risk ŌĆö they use `.shared` synchronously and don't suspend on waiters). **Severity Medium** ŌĆö DebugBridge is DEBUG-only (not in Release); latent test-flake risk. **FIXED 2026-05-19** (branch `fix/issue-939-debugreader-await-isolation`): `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests.makeRegistry()` now returns `DebugReaderRegistry.makeIsolatedForTests()` (the DEBUG-only factory added by bug #227 / PR #940) ŌĆö each `@Test` owns its own registry, no shared mutable state, and the `reset()` call is dropped (a fresh instance starts empty). **RED**: new `bug228_concurrentResetOnSiblingRegistry_doesNotCancelOwnWaiter` stands up two registry contexts itself and proves a `reset()` on one cannot spuriously time out a suspended `awaitReader` on the other. The "latent" framing was conservative ŌĆö verified RED on the pre-fix code: the new test failed its `registryA !== registryB` assertion (both were `.shared`) AND its background `reset()` cross-cancelled `case2`/`case5`'s suspended waiters, empirically showing the defect was one `reset()`-calling test away from manifesting suite-wide. **Verified GREEN**: focused `DebugReaderRegistryAwaitReaderTests` passes 7/7, **3/3 consecutive** full-suite runs, deterministic. Broader `-only-testing:vreaderTests` run hit the pre-existing #221-class flaky parallel-pool crash (1 host-process crash, varying location, 0 real assertion failures ŌĆö reproduced identically on pristine `origin/main` `d37bcc1` with zero of this fix's changes), independent of this fix. Production `DebugReaderRegistry.swift` not modified ŌĆö test-side-only fix. `RealDebugBridgeContextTests` / `DebugReaderRegistryTests` left untouched (out of this issue's AC; both are `XCTestCase`, which runs methods serially per class, so they cannot suspend a sibling's `waiters` continuation under parallelism ŌĆö genuinely lower-risk, optional follow-up). Codex audit `019e3f4d`, 1 round, ship-as-is (`.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-939-debugreader-await-isolation-audit.md`). GH: #939 |
| 226| `TTSService.rate` `didSet` infinite recursion ŌĆö its clamping `didSet` re-assigns the property, which under `@Observable` re-enters the synthesized setter forever ŌåÆ stack overflow / test-host crash | Services/TTS | Medium | FIXED | **Renumbered 225 ŌåÆ 226 on 2026-05-19**: GH #910 and GH #911 were filed concurrently by two different agents and BOTH titled themselves "Bug #225", colliding two rows in this file. Resolved per the #64/#70 feature-collision precedent ŌĆö this row (GH #910, the TTS recursion) takes the next free number 226; the separate TXT test-isolation row keeps 225 (GH #911). **Filed 2026-05-19 by the feature #57 (AZW3/MOBI TTS) implementation run** while running the WI-1 test gate. `TTSService` is `@MainActor @Observable` (`vreader/Services/TTS/TTSService.swift:19-20`). `rate`'s `didSet` (`:34-36`) does `rate = min(max(rate, 0.0), 1.0)` to clamp. The `@Observable` macro rewrites a `didSet`-bearing stored property into a **computed** `rate` over backing `_rate`; the `didSet` lives on `_rate`. The body's `rate = ŌĆ”` calls the **computed** setter ŌåÆ sets `_rate` ŌåÆ fires `didSet` again ŌĆö Swift's didSet-self-assignment suppression does not span the computedŌåÆstored boundary, so it recurses unboundedly. **Exact same defect class as Bug #222** (`ReaderSettingsStore.autoPageTurnInterval`) ŌĆö a *different* property on a *different* `@Observable` class; #222's fix did not catch this instance. **Repro**: `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/TTSServiceSpeedControlTests -parallel-testing-enabled NO` on iPhone 17 Pro Sim ŌĆö `speedControl_defaultRate()` (reads `rate` only) passes; the 5 rate-*mutating* tests (`speedControl_setsRate_low/_high`, `speedControl_clampsAboveMax/_clampsBelowMin`, `speedControl_rateAppliedToUtterance`) crash the test process (`Restarting after unexpected exit, crash, or test timeout`). Confirmed pre-existing on pristine `origin/main` at commit `42908c4`. **Two-fold impact**: (1) test-gate reliability ŌĆö the 5 `TTSServiceSpeedControlTests` reliably crash the full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` run, verdict `** TEST FAILED **` despite the Swift Testing summary reporting 1073 tests passed; (2) latent product defect ŌĆö any runtime assignment to `TTSService.rate` (a speech-rate settings control) crashes the app; the recursion does not fire during `init` (Swift suppresses observers there), which is why it was not caught earlier. **Fix direction**: mirror Bug #222's fix and `TTSService`'s sibling pattern ŌĆö convert `rate` to a computed `get`/`set` pair over a private `_rate`, clamping in `set`; no `didSet`, no observer re-entry; `init` assigns the backing var directly. NOT fixed by the feature #57 run ŌĆö #57 does not touch `TTSService` (out of scope per its plan ┬¦3.4). **FIXED 2026-05-19** (PR #934, branch `fix/issue-910-ttsservice-rate-recursion`, v3.34.13): `rate` converted from a stored property with a clamping `didSet` to a computed `get`/`set` pair over a new `private var _rate: Float = 0.5`, clamping in `set` (`set { _rate = min(max(newValue, 0.0), 1.0) }`) ŌĆö no `didSet`, no `` setter re-entry. Mirrors the Bug #222 fix and the sibling `ReaderSettingsStore.backgroundOpacity`. RED test `TTSServiceSpeedControlTests.speedControl_inRangeAssignmentDoesNotRecurse` (same-value post-init re-assignment ŌĆö the tightest recursion repro); the 5 pre-existing rate-mutating tests were already RED. Test gate: focused `TTSServiceSpeedControlTests` passes 7/7 post-fix (verified pre-fix RED on pristine `origin/main` ŌĆö `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/TTSServiceSpeedControlTests` reports `** TEST FAILED **` / `Test run with 0 tests` because the recursion crashes the host before any test reports). Full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` run no longer SIGSEGVs from TTS ŌĆö runs to ~3516 tests vs. the baseline crashing at ~669; the residual single `** TEST FAILED **` is the pre-existing #221-class flaky parallel-pool crash (1 crash, varying location, zero assertion failures ŌĆö reproduced identically on pristine `origin/main`), independent of this fix and already characterised under Bug #225's known-timing-flake note. Codex audit `019e3ee8`, 1 round, ship-as-is; `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-910-ttsservice-rate-recursion-audit.md`. GH: #910 |

| 108| AZW3/Foliate reader: center tap does not toggle chrome (REOPENED 2026-05-20 ŌĆö regression)             | Foliate/* | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-21 (v3.39.1, branch `fix/issue-224-azw3-center-tap-chrome`)** ŌĆö root cause was a coordinate-space mismatch introduced by the Bug #239 fix (`bd7564c7`), NOT the bilingual-injection hypothesis in the original reopen note (device diagnosis confirmed the bilingual path does in-place DOM `insertBefore` and never reloads the doc; the click listener already re-binds on every Foliate `load`). In **paginated** mode foliate-js renders a section as a 2-column page inside an iframe ~2├Ś the screen width and pages by shifting that iframe horizontally via its element `left` (device-confirmed: `left: -359` over a 402px host viewport) to reveal one column. The Bug #239 content-tap handler posted `{x: event.clientX, w: documentElement.clientWidth}` ŌĆö but `event.clientX` is in the iframe's internal coordinate space (0..748) while `documentElement.clientWidth` is a single column (374). So `ReaderTapZoneRouter` saw `x/w Ōłł ~1.0..2.0` on every right-column page and classified a center tap as a right-zone tap ŌåÆ `.readerNextPage` instead of `.readerContentTapped`; the toolbar never toggled (and on the right edge the tap turned the page). EPUB was unaffected because it renders in the top-level document (no nested iframe ŌåÆ `clientX`/`clientWidth` already host-relative). **Fix**: new `mapTapToHostViewport(doc, clientX)` in `foliate-host.js` maps the click back to host-viewport coords ŌĆö `hostX = clientX + frameElement.getBoundingClientRect().left`, `hostW = frameElement.ownerDocument.defaultView.innerWidth`; no host frame ŌåÆ `documentElement.clientWidth` (top-level case); unusable host width / cross-origin ŌåÆ returns `null` so the handler posts the bare chrome-toggle `tap` (safe default). `foliate-bundle.js` rebuilt via `build-bundle.sh`. **Device-verified (iPhone 17 Pro Sim iOS 26.5, UDID `1FAB9493ŌĆ”`, mini-azw3 paginated, right-column page `frameLeft=-359`)**: the live production handler, captured via the real `webkit.messageHandlers.tap.postMessage`, posts `{x:201,w:402}` for a screen-center tap ŌåÆ `0.50` ŌåÆ center/TOGGLE; screen-left(15%) ŌåÆ `{x:60,w:402}` ŌåÆ left/prev; screen-right(85%) ŌåÆ `{x:341,w:402}` ŌåÆ right/next (Bug #239 side-tap preserved). Regression guard `FoliateHostTapCoordinateTests` pins both source + built bundle with comment-stripped executable-pattern assertions. Codex Gate-4 audit: 2 rounds, ship-as-is (`.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-224-azw3-center-tap-chrome-audit.md`). **REOPENED 2026-05-20 (user triage ŌĆö "can not see the tool bar by tapping on the center")**. The original fix (FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator's `handleMessage(name:"tap")` posting `.readerContentTapped`) IS still in place at `vreader/Views/Reader/FoliateSpikeView.swift:617-623`; the JS producer is still at `vreader/Services/Foliate/JS/foliate-host.js:120` (`post('tap', {})` from a doc-level `click` listener attached on `view.addEventListener('load', ...)`). User reports center-tap no longer toggles the toolbar on AZW3. Strong suspect: feature #56 WI-11 (`e8c1c2e4` ŌĆö `FoliateBilingualContainerView`) or WI-15 (`5adc346b` ŌĆö re-translation) injection breaks the click-listener chain. The bilingual JS injects `<div class="vreader-bilingual" data-vreader-decoration>` blocks after each source paragraph; if injection reloads or replaces the doc, the `click` listener (attached once at `view.load`) does not re-attach to the new doc and the `post('tap', {})` never fires. Cross-ref: Bug #246 (AZW3 wrong-reader-UI) filed concurrently ŌĆö if both share root cause, Bug #246's fix lands first and #108's repro should be retested. **Fix direction**: re-bind the doc-level click listener every time the Foliate view emits a `load` event (not just on initial), OR delegate the click capture to a higher-level listener that survives doc replacement. **Original fix history (still valid as a contract)**: Toolbar stayed visible on center tap in FoliateSpikeView (the AZW3 reader). EPUB chrome toggle worked. **FIXED** by adding `case "tap":` to FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator's message handler that posts `.readerContentTapped` ŌĆö the notification ReaderContainerView already observes to call `toggleChrome()`. Root cause: the JS bundle's `tap` message hit the default branch and no-oped. Refactored: extracted Coordinator from inside `FoliateSpikeWebView` (private struct) into a top-level extension so the new `handleMessage(name:body:)` method is unit-testable without constructing a real `WKScriptMessage`. Verified by `FoliateSpikeViewTapTests.tapMessage_postsReaderContentTappedNotification`. Codex audit: 1 round + 1 followup, ship-as-is. GH: #224 |

| 146| Late-attached observer misses debugBridgeThemeChanged on reader-mount                                 | DevTools/*| Low      | WONT FIX    | Originally filed by Codex audit on bug #144 fix as a theoretical first-mount race. **Re-investigated 2026-05-06; not a real race** ŌĆö `RealDebugBridgeContext.theme(_:_:)` writes UserDefaults BEFORE posting the notification (via `store.theme = target` whose `didSet` calls `defaults.set`). When a fresh `ReaderContainerView` mounts, its `@State settingsStore = ReaderSettingsStore()` initializer reads UserDefaults at view-init ŌĆö which already has the new value. The "missed notification" is redundant for a fresh-mount case. UserDefaults is the source of truth at init; the notification is a live-update primitive for an EXISTING reader. Reconcile-from-defaults safety net was prototyped on `fix/issue-320-reconcile-from-defaults` and reverted unmerged after this analysis: the simulated race didn't actually demonstrate the fix because UserDefaults backstops the scenario. Closing as WONT FIX. GH: #320 |

| 148| `decodeWithHint_fallsBack_whenHintEncodingFailsToDecode` test broken: 24-byte UTF-8 input is even-length, so UTF-16 hint silently decodes to gibberish | Reader/*  | Low      | FIXED       | **FIXED**: test renamed `..._whenHintEncodingIsUnknown` and rewritten to trigger the fallback via `encodingFromName` returning nil (unknown hint name "ZZZ-NotReal") instead of via decoder-rejects-bytes. Foundation's `String(data:, encoding: .utf16)` is lenient: it accepts any even-byte payload (silently drops trailing odd byte) and returns UTF-16 code units regardless of content, so the original premise (odd-byte input ŌåÆ UTF-16 returns nil) was wrong ŌĆö a 13-byte payload still decoded to 6 chars. The unknown-name path is the only reliable trigger for the fallback in a unit test. Added `#expect(encodingFromName(hintName) == nil)` guard so future aliasing fails loudly. Codex audit: 2 rounds, ship-as-is. Both Lows (rename for accuracy + aliasing guard) addressed in round 2. GH: #338 |

EPUB marks settled from `EPUBWebViewBridge.Coordinator.webView(_:didFinish:)` (page-load complete); AZW3/MOBI from the Foliate `relocate` message (`FoliateSpikeView.Coordinator` ŌĆö the live host ŌĆö gained a `relocate` case; `FoliateViewCoordinator`'s existing `relocate` case also marks). `relocate` is the real render-complete signal ŌĆö `didFinish` is just the HTML shell before foliate-js paginates. `ReaderContainerView.onAppear` wires `probe.settleStrategy` for `.epub`/`.azw3`; TXT/MD/PDF keep the 100ms `Task.sleep` fallback (out of scope). | 154| Search-tap navigation in TXT reader skips temporary yellow highlight at destination (bug #43 contract regression) | Reader/*  | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-19** (branch `fix/issue-443-search-nav-highlight-renav`). Implements the runtime-traced root cause from the 2026-05-18 trace below: a search-nav to an already-current target re-sets `uiState.highlightRange` / `scrollToOffset` to values they already hold ŌåÆ `@Observable` no-op write ŌåÆ SwiftUI body never re-evaluates ŌåÆ bridge `updateUIView` never runs ŌåÆ temp highlight never re-painted. **Fix**: added a monotonic `highlightNonce: Int` to `TextReaderUIState` (and the `ReaderNotificationHandlerStateProtocol`), bumped on every navigate event by `ReaderNotificationHandlers.handleNavigateToLocator` (`&+=`, after the nil-offset guard). `TXTTextViewBridge` + `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` fold a nonce change into their highlight-change detection via the new pure static `TXTTextViewBridge.highlightShouldReapply(rangeChanged:nonceChanged:)`, so a repeat-nav re-paints + re-arms the 3 s auto-clear timer even when the NSRange is byte-for-byte identical. `ReaderNotificationModifier` was switched from a duplicate inline copy of the navigate logic to call the extracted, unit-tested `handleNavigateToLocator` (removes the duplication that caused the nonce bump to be missed). The original verify-cron analysis conflated two distinct concerns: (a) orphan `@State` in non-chapter paths (real, this PR addresses, with regression-guard tests); (b) WI-7 chapter-mode globalŌåÆlocal offset translation (deferred feature work, no fixture yet exercises the non-chapter paths to runtime-verify (a) directly). MD reader is unaffected because MD does not have a chapter-mode renderer branch. **Filed by verify cron 2026-05-08T22:57** during feature #2 (Highlight search result at destination) round-2 verification. Sibling to bug #153: while #153 fixed the SCROLL POSITION (matched text now lands inside the viewport with 25% top headroom), the temporary yellow highlight on the matched range itself NEVER renders for TXT files. Reproducible end-to-end on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.14.92: launch with `--seed-position-test --reset-preferences`, open Position Test Book, tap search ŌåÆ paste "Paragraph 50" ŌåÆ tap result. Reader scrolls correctly to paragraph 50 (#153 fix working), but no `UIColor.systemYellow.withAlphaComponent(0.4)` background appears on "Paragraph 50" before the 3s auto-clear timer would fire. Two artifacts saved (`feature-2-r2-after-search-tap-paragraph50-20260508.png` + `feature-2-r2-immediately-after-tap-20260508.png`). Root cause (code-read confirmed): `TXTReaderContainerView.swift` declares two `highlightRange` states ŌĆö line 62 has a local `@State private var highlightRange: NSRange?` that's read by `readerContent` (line 471) and `chapterReaderContent` (line 526) but **never assigned anywhere**, while line 78's `@State var uiState = TextReaderUIState()` exposes `uiState.highlightRange` (the one `ReaderNotificationModifier.swift:34-47` actually sets when `.readerNavigateToLocator` fires). `MDReaderContainerView.swift:312` reads `uiState.highlightRange` (correct wiring); the TXT container reads the orphan local @State. Net effect: search-tap notification updates `uiState.highlightRange`, but `TXTTextViewBridge` is fed the orphan `@State` so `applyHighlights` is a no-op for the active range. Affects every TXT search; PDF/EPUB/Foliate paths use their own renderer and are not affected. Fix sketch: delete the orphan `@State` at lines 62 + 65, replace `highlightRange: highlightRange` and `highlightIsTemporary: highlightIsTemporary` at 471/472 + 526/527 with `uiState.highlightRange` / `uiState.highlightIsTemporary`. Add an integration test asserting that posting `.readerNavigateToLocator` with a TXT locator results in the bridge's active highlight range matching the locator's `charRangeStartUTF16/charRangeEndUTF16`. Cross-ref: feature #2 evidence at `dev-docs/verification/feature-2-20260508.md`. **Bugfix-cron diagnostic round 2026-05-18** (deep code-read responding to the REOPENED note's "trace the round-trip" mandate ŌĆö no runtime trace yet, no code shipped). **(1) Range translation PROVEN correct, ruled OUT as the cause**: within a single `chapterReaderContent` render (`TXTReaderContainerView.swift:569`), `chapterLocalScrollOffset` and `chapterLocalHighlightRanges` take the *same* `viewModel.currentChapterIdx` + chapters, and `uiState.scrollToOffset == uiState.highlightRange.location` (both = `resolveTXT`'s `globalStart` ŌĆö `SearchHitToLocatorResolver.resolveTXT` sets `charOffsetUTF16 == charRangeStartUTF16 == segBase + matchStart`, `ReaderNotificationModifier:37-42` copies them). So scroll-translation-succeeds Ō¤╣ highlight-temp-translation-succeeds in that render; `TXTChapterHighlightHelper.highlightsForChapter`'s clip math is sound. The symptom "scroll works, highlight doesn't" therefore is NOT the globalŌåÆchapter-local translation. **(2) Concrete defect found ŌĆö `TXTTextViewBridge.makeUIView`**: it seeds `coordinator.persistedHighlights` from the param (`TXTTextViewBridge.swift:101`) but does NOT seed `coordinator.currentHighlightRange` from the `highlightRange` param. `makeUIView`'s initial `applyHighlights` (line 108, commented "set highlights first so drawBackground has correct ranges") thus paints `active: nil` ŌĆö the temp/search highlight is dropped on a fresh bridge's first render. **(3) Why chapter-mode-specific**: chapter-mode search-nav swaps `chapterAttrString` nilŌåÆloadingViewŌåÆback (`TXTReaderContainerView.swift:595-601`), so SwiftUI creates a FRESH `TXTTextViewBridge` per chapter (fresh coordinator, `currentHighlightRange` defaults nil). Non-chapter `readerContent`/`chunkedReaderContent` keep ONE bridge identity for the whole doc, so their `updateUIView` always carries the highlight ŌĆö that is why TXT-non-chapter + MD are unaffected. **(4) Not yet pinned**: whether seeding `currentHighlightRange` in `makeUIView` (symmetric with line 101) is the *complete* fix, or whether a second `updateUIView` highlightChanged-timing factor remains ŌĆö needs the `Logger` runtime trace of `makeUIView`/`updateUIView`/`chapterReaderContent` against `--seed-position-test` that the REOPENED note asked for. **Do NOT ship a code-read-only fix** ŌĆö this bug was already twice "code-complete but runtime-incomplete" (PARTIAL FIX, then WI-3); the next bugfix iteration must runtime-trace first, then fix + RED/GREEN test + device-verify. Status stays REOPENED. **Bugfix-cron runtime trace 2026-05-18 (the mandated trace ŌĆö DONE; supersedes diagnoses (1)-(4) above).** Instrumented `Logger` traces across the full chain (`readerNavigateToLocator`ŌåÆ`chapterLocalHighlightRanges`ŌåÆ`updateUIView`ŌåÆ`setHighlightRanges`ŌåÆ`HighlightingLayoutManager.drawBackground`), built + installed on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4), ran the `--seed-position-test` repro 3├Ś. **Finding A ŌĆö the highlight DOES render; the makeUIView-asymmetry hypothesis (2) is WRONG.** Run 1 (first search-tap, reader scrolls topŌåÆPara 50): the full chain fires ŌĆö `chapterLocalHighlightRanges tempGlobalRange={8847,12} chapterIndex=0 ŌåÆ temp={8847,12}` (chapter translation correct, confirming (1)); `updateUIView highlightChanged=true`; `setHighlightRanges active={8847,12} numberOfGlyphs=18027`; then `drawBackground searchHighlightRange={8847,12} ŌĆ” visibleGlyphIntersect.len=12` (the `paint()` yellow-fill *executes*); then `setHighlightRanges active=nil` exactly 3.0s later (auto-clear timer). The temporary highlight renders correctly for the full 3s window. `makeUIView` runs once at app launch with `highlightRange=nil`; search-nav is delivered via `updateUIView` which seeds + paints correctly ŌĆö so the `makeUIView`/`currentHighlightRange` asymmetry is a harmless latent inconsistency, NOT this bug. **Finding B ŌĆö the real defect: a repeat-nav produces no view update.** Runs 2 & 3 (re-tap the same search result while the reader is ALREADY at that location): `readerNavigateToLocator` fires and re-sets `uiState.highlightRange={8847,12}` ŌĆö but **zero downstream chain** (no `chapterLocalHighlightRanges`/`updateUIView`/`setHighlightRanges`/`drawBackground` logged at all). Cause: the `.readerNavigateToLocator` handler (`ReaderNotificationModifier.swift:37-46`) sets `uiState.scrollToOffset` / `highlightIsTemporary` / `highlightRange` all to the values they ALREADY hold ŌĆö the prior nav left them set, and the 3s auto-clear clears only the bridge coordinator's `currentHighlightRange`, never `uiState.highlightRange`. With no observable change, `TXTReaderContainerView.body` does not re-evaluate ŌåÆ `updateUIView` is never called ŌåÆ the temp highlight is never re-applied. Run 1 only worked because the SCROLL itself drove the re-render. **Why verify-cron repeatedly saw "no highlight":** (a) computer-use screenshots taken via a model round-trip after the tap routinely land *past* the 3s auto-clear window ŌĆö reproduced exactly in this round's run 1 (screenshot at tap+~4s, highlight already cleared); and/or (b) repeated repro attempts on the same paragraph (round-2: 4 attempts; round-3: re-ran "Paragraph 50"/"Paragraph 100") hit Finding B from the 2nd attempt onward. **Corrected root cause:** the bug is real, but the trigger is "search-nav to an already-current target," NOT "first search." The filed first-search repro is not itself a product defect ŌĆö it is a screenshot-timing artifact. **Fix direction (NOT shipped this iteration):** make the temporary search highlight re-apply on every `.readerNavigateToLocator` regardless of whether `uiState` values changed ŌĆö e.g. a monotonic nonce on `TextReaderUIState` bumped by the handler and treated like `highlightChanged` by the TXT/chunked/MD bridges, and/or have the 3s auto-clear also clear `uiState.highlightRange` so a re-nav becomes a genuine nilŌåÆvalue transition. Cross-cutting (`TextReaderUIState` + `ReaderNotificationModifier` + `TXTTextViewBridge` + `TXTChunkedReaderBridge` + `MDReaderContainerView`) ŌĆö a proper multi-file TDD fix, not a patch. This iteration ran the mandated trace only; no code shipped (instrumentation reverted, fix branch dropped); the CU display went unavailable mid-session so a behavioral UI fix cannot be device-verified now ŌĆö fix deferred to a future bugfix iteration. Status stays REOPENED. GH: #443 |

CSS `column-width` is a **hint** (minimum desired width) ŌĆö the browser creates as many columns as fit. When the viewport width / book CSS combination allowed two columns to fit (e.g. book stylesheet pushed body width beyond the viewport), the browser packed two columns. **FIXED 2026-05-12**: added `column-count: 1 !important` to the body CSS. Round-1 audit (Codex thread `019e1827-04bd-7593-96a1-59f78fea2030`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is) escalated the defense to mark the FULL pagination param set reader-owned via `!important` (column-count, column-width, column-gap, column-fill, height, and html+body overflow) ŌĆö so book CSS `!important` on column-width or height can't desynchronize `scrollWidth / viewportWidth` and break paging math. Round-1 finding [3] also tightened a pre-existing tiny-viewport gap: `column-width` and `height` now clamp to `max(_, 1)` / `max(_, 0)` to prevent negative-px emission during Stage Manager / split-screen resize storms. Round-1 finding [2] (WKWebView runtime integration test) ACCEPTED as out of scope ŌĆö vreaderTests has no precedent for WKWebView rendering integration; structural tests pin the exact `!important` contract and post-merge device verification exercises the rendered behaviour. 3 new regression-guard tests (column-count !important at portrait + landscape viewports, tiny-viewport clamp) + updates to existing column-fill assertion. 30/30 EPUBPagination tests pass on iPhone 17 Pro Simulator. | 169| AI Settings expanded sections (API Key / Provider Configuration / Data & Privacy) don't render after flipping toggle ON until app relaunch | Settings/AI | Medium | FIXED | **NOTE on numbering**: GH issue title says "Bug #167" because the verify-cron filing this didn't consult the local tracker ŌĆö the EPUB rubber-band bug was already row #167. Assigning local row #169 (next available) and renaming the GH issue title to match. **Root cause**: `AISettingsViewModel.isAIEnabled` was a pure get/set computed property delegating to `FeatureFlags.isEnabled(.aiAssistant)` / `setOverride(_:for:)`. The `@Observable` macro only instruments stored properties ŌĆö a computed property whose body reads/writes a non-Observable class bypasses `_$observationRegistrar` entirely on both read and write. Result: in `AISettingsSection`, the conditional `if viewModel.isAIEnabled { /* API Key, Provider Configuration, Data & Privacy */ }` never re-evaluated after the toggle's setter wrote through ŌĆö SwiftUI didn't know to invalidate the view. The flag DID persist to UserDefaults; the conditional just didn't re-render. Only an app kill+relaunch re-initialized the view model from FeatureFlags on first render, picking up the new value. **Fix**: convert `isAIEnabled` from computed to stored property with a `didSet` write-through. Seed `self.isAIEnabled = featureFlags.isEnabled(.aiAssistant)` once at init time. The `@Observable` macro now instruments the stored property's storage ŌĆö writes fire `_$observationRegistrar.withMutation`, reads call `_$observationRegistrar.access`, so SwiftUI's `if viewModel.isAIEnabled` block re-renders on the next runloop tick after toggle. The `oldValue != isAIEnabled` guard dedupes the WRITE-THROUGH (and resulting UserDefaults write) on same-value assignments. FeatureFlags' `Sendable` concurrency contract unchanged ŌĆö fix is local to `AISettingsViewModel`. Codex MCP audit `019e13c8` (2 rounds): round 1 found 1 Medium (over-asserting test about `@Observable` same-value behavior ŌĆö replaced with a sentinel-value UserDefaults test pinning the write-through dedup contract) + 1 Low (comment overclaim ŌĆö rescoped to write-through, not re-renders); round 2 zero new findings, ship-as-is. | 168| EPUB font family setting has no effect ŌĆö `fontFamily` never injected into CSS | Reader/EPUB | High | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-10** during user-reported issue. `ReaderTheme.epubOverrideCSS` had no `fontFamily` parameter; the call site in `EPUBReaderContainerView` only passed fontSize/lineHeight/letterSpacing ŌĆö `typography.fontFamily` was stored, persisted, and surfaced in the AA picker correctly but never reached the WKWebView CSS. **FIXED** by adding `fontFamily: ReaderFontFamily = .system` parameter + a `cssFontStack(for:)` helper that maps `.system` ŌåÆ `-apple-system, system-ui, sans-serif`, `.serif` ŌåÆ `Georgia, 'Times New Roman', serif`, `.monospace` ŌåÆ `'SF Mono', Menlo, 'Courier New', monospace`. The face is declared on `html, body` and forced on every descendant via `body * { font-family: inherit !important; }` so per-element book-CSS rules can't beat the user's pick. `pre`/`code`/`samp`/`kbd` and their descendants are pinned to a semantic monospace stack (`ui-monospace, 'SF Mono', Menlo, 'Courier New', monospace !important`) so code blocks stay legible regardless of body-font choice. CJK fallback is automatic: Latin-only faces (Georgia, Menlo, etc.) carry no CJK glyphs, so the platform falls through to the system CJK font. **Residual gap (accepted)**: inline `style="font-family: ... !important"` and pseudo-element `::before`/`::after` font-family declarations still win ŌĆö both are rare in real EPUBs and out of scope for this fix. Codex MCP audit `019e11a0` (3 rounds): round 1 found 1 High (cascade strength) + 1 Medium (test strength) + 1 Low (comment mismatch); round 2 found 1 Medium (cascade still bypassable for `a`/`em`/`strong` etc., suggested broad sweep) + 1 Medium (tests still string-level, stale comment); round 3 found 1 Medium (doc claim too broad ŌĆö narrowed to acknowledge inline-author-important + pseudo gaps) + 1 Low (assertion strength); all fixed. | 159| EPUB highlights save to data layer but don't visually render on the page (CSS Highlight API not painting yellow background) | EPUB/*    | Medium   | FIXED | **FIXED via two-part change addressing both the root cause and a latent issue surfaced during diagnosis**: (1) **XPath namespace rewrite in `resolveNodeFromXPath`** (root cause): EPUB chapters load as `application/xhtml+xml` so `documentElement.namespaceURI` is `http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml`. XPath 1.0 element names without a namespace prefix don't match XHTML-namespaced elements, so `getXPath`-produced paths like `/html/body/p[3]/text()[1]` returned null, `buildRange` returned null, and `__vreader_createHighlight` early-returned BEFORE either render path executed. Fix rewrites element-name segments to `*[local-name()="name"]` when document has a namespace; preserves `text()`, `comment()`, `node()` axis tokens; handles prefix-qualified names like `svg:svg` (Codex audit round-1 Medium fix). (2) **CSS Highlight API now primary, SVG Overlayer fallback** (visibility): even with valid Range, the SVG Overlayer paints rectangles in document coords into a 100%-tall SVG positioned over `<html>`. In paged EPUB mode (CSS multi-column layout), document y > viewport-height is clipped from the SVG's viewport even though the text appears in the next column visually ŌĆö rect drawn but invisible. CSS Highlight API renders at text-paint time and follows column transforms automatically. Swapped the priority order. (3) **foliate-bridge.js DOMContentLoaded timing fix** (defensive): script is injected at `.atDocumentEnd` which runs AFTER DOMContentLoaded fires, so the auto-setup listener never executed and `window.__foliate.overlayer` stayed undefined. Replaced with `if (document.readyState === 'loading') addEventListener(...) else __vreader_setupFoliate()` so setup runs synchronously when past loading state. Codex MCP audit (thread `019e0c82`, 2 rounds): round 1 found 1 Medium (regex didn't handle prefix-qualified names) ŌĆö fixed. Round 2 ship-as-is. Test gate: 748/748 unit tests pass. New regression-guard tests: 3 new in `EPUBHighlightBridgeTests` (`highlightAPIJS_rewritesXPathForXHTMLNamespace`, `highlightAPIJS_preservesNonElementSteps`, `highlightAPIJS_handlesPrefixedElementNames`) pinning the source-token markers for the namespace rewrite + prefix strip. Also fixed pre-existing stale test `txtFormat_canUseUnified_whenSettingIsUnified` from bug #158's #468 regression (renamed to `txtFormat_cannotUseUnified_evenWhenSettingIsUnified` and inverted to pin post-#158 contract). Codex audit `019e2d96`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is ŌĆö round 1 raised 3 Lows (2 comment-drift items in shared contract + presenter header, 1 missing gesture-wrapper integration test); round 2 fixed the 2 doc Lows and accepted the test gap with rationale (1-line UIKit `convert(_:to:)` call against framework-tested code; pure-point overload IS pinned). Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-743-uieditmenu-coord-space-audit.md`. **Originally filed by verify-cron 2026-05-16** during Feature #53 round-2 device-verify on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.5) at v3.23.3 (commit 3026aa1, post-Bug-#202-fix). Bug #202's chrome-toggle suppression IS confirmed: tap on yellow "Prince"/"Pavlovna's" does NOT toggle chrome (hit-test path fires + early-return suppresses fall-through). However `presenter.present(...)` is invoked but the `UIEditMenuInteraction` popover never visibly appears. Two confirmation screenshots (CU + `simctl io`) both show no menu. **Likely root cause**: `UIEditMenuConfiguration.sourcePoint` expects interaction-view coordinate space, but `TXTTextViewBridge.Coordinator.resolveHighlightTap` returns `event.sourceRect` as window-space (`textView.convert(viewRect, to: nil)`). Mismatch puts the popover at unpredictable view-space coordinates ŌĆö likely off-screen. **Why not caught before**: pre-Bug-#202-fix, chapter-mode TXT didn't reach `presenter.present(...)` at all because the lookup was empty. Chrome-toggle masked the menu invisibility. Bug #202 fix exposed this latent bug. Unit tests use `FakePresenter` that bypasses the real `UIEditMenuInteraction` code path. **Affects**: Feature #53 acceptance criterion (a) for TXT minimum; likely MD/EPUB/PDF too (same presenter, same potential mismatch). Foliate (Bug #199 fix) uses `sourceRect: .zero` intentionally so its issue is "anchored at view origin" not "invisible" ŌĆö separate known follow-up. **Fix direction**: convert window-space ŌåÆ view-space at `UIKitHighlightActionPresenter.present(for:in:)` via `view.convert(rect, from: nil)`, OR change `event.sourceRect` semantics to always be view-space at the bridge layer. Add regression test in `HighlightActionPresenterTests` for the coordinate-space contract. GH: #743 |

| 197| Library view does not auto-refresh after Feature #59 file-URL import ŌĆö book appears only after cold-restart | App/*, Library/* | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-16** in branch `fix/issue-708-library-no-auto-refresh-import`. Root cause: `FileURLImportRouter.dispatch()` (Feature #59 WI-2) called `BookImporter.importFile()` which inserted into SwiftData but no signal reached the library view. `LibraryView` uses an imperative `LibraryViewModel.books` array refilled by `loadBooks()`, not a reactive `@Query`, so the new row stayed invisible until the next cold launch (the in-app Files-picker path worked because `LibraryViewModel.importFiles()` explicitly calls `loadBooks()` after import). Fix: `BookImporter` now posts `Notification.Name.bookDidImport` (with `userInfo: ["fingerprintKey": String]`) after both the new-insert AND duplicate-replace paths. `LibraryView` observes it via a dedicated `BookDidImportRefresher` ViewModifier (extracted because adding the observer inline pushed the LibraryView body past the Swift type-checker's complexity limit) and triggers `viewModel.refresh(force: true)`. Plus a coalescing refactor to `LibraryViewModel.refresh(force:)`: the previous behavior dropped re-entrant calls (`guard !isRefreshing else { return }`); the new behavior drains pending work via `repeat { hasPendingRefresh = false; await loadBooks() } while hasPendingRefresh && iterations < 8`, with a follow-up `Task { @MainActor [weak self] in await self?.refresh(force: true) }` fallback if the 8-iteration safety bound trips. Codex audit `019e2cd7`, 4 rounds, ship-as-is. 29 tests in `BookImporterNotificationTests` + `LibraryViewModelTests` (including new `refreshConcurrentCalls_coalesceIntoTrailingRefresh` + `refreshThreeWaveCoalesce_drainsUntilQuiescent`). Caller `ReaderSearchCoordinator.setup(...)` creates the coordinator as a local, awaits `enqueueBookIndexing(...)`, then returns ŌĆö local reference drops and `[weak self]` allows the actor to be deallocated BEFORE the detached background task starts running. By task-start time, `self?` is nil and `processQueue` never runs. EPUB exposed this more than TXT because `EPUBParser.open(...)` + spine iteration + `parser.close()` adds enough delay before setup() returns that the coordinator dies before scheduling resolves; TXT happened to win the race more often (synchronous `Data(contentsOf:)` + smaller fixture). Fix: change `[weak self]` to strong `self` capture in the detached task. The actor's invariant ("we must drain pendingJobs once isProcessing flips true") makes strong-self correct ŌĆö the task voluntarily releases the strong reference when `processQueue` returns. Regression test `enqueueIndexing_processesEvenWhenCallerDropsCoordinator` directly reproduces the bug: pre-fix `callCount == 0`, post-fix `callCount == 1`. | 183| TXT search panel freezes UI on first open ŌĆö enqueueBookIndexing inherits @MainActor, calls TXTTextExtractor.extractWithOffsets (blocking file I/O + encoding detection) on main thread | Reader/TXT | Medium | FIXED | **Reported by user 2026-05-14**. | 182| EPUB search: cross-chapter result tap navigates to chapter top but no yellow highlight visible ŌĆö Locator.textQuote contained the raw search snippet (`...prefix<b>match</b>suffix...`), plain-text matcher couldn't find the literal HTML in the DOM (round 2: snippet-markup defect FIXED; round 3 needed for deferred-eval pipeline silence in user-tap flow) | Reader/EPUB | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-18 (round-3, GH #621)** ŌĆö round-1 (defer JS to didFinish) and round-2 (`cleanSnippetForTextQuote` snippet-markup strip, below) both landed but the symptom persisted: verify-cron round-5 DOM-probes proved the `.vreader_search_highlight` span is never injected via the user-tap pipeline. Round-3 root cause ŌĆö `EPUBHighlightBridge.searchHighlightJS` ran `window.find()` exactly once, synchronously at `webView(_:didFinish:)`; at that instant the freshly-loaded chapter has not finished its post-load relayout (foliate-js `cssPreprocessJS`, a `WKUserScript` injected `atDocumentEnd`, rewrites every `-epub-*`/`page-break-*` rule), so `window.find()` returns false and no span is created. The Swift stashŌåÆconsume pipeline was already correct. **Fix** (JS-only, `searchHighlightJS`): poll `window.find()` on a bounded 50ms retry loop (40 attempts Ōēł 2s) until the rendered DOM is searchable; a `window.__vreaderSearchHighlightGen` generation token supersedes concurrent retry loops; the wrap-and-insert is `try/catch`-guarded. 4 new structural unit tests in `EPUBHighlightBridgeTests`. Codex audit `019e3959` (3 rounds ŌĆö 1 Medium + 4 Low all fixed ŌĆö ship-as-is); audit log `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-621-epub-cross-chapter-highlight-r3-audit.md`. The retry's real runtime behavior isn't unit-testable; post-merge close-gate re-runs the cross-chapter search-tap repro with a `vreader-debug://eval?bridge=epub` DOM probe (CU-free) ŌĆö `awaiting-device-verification`. ŌĆö **FIXED 2026-05-15** (round-2 root cause) ŌĆö the round-1 v3.21.50 deferred-eval mechanism (`pendingHighlightJS` stash + didFinish consume on the coordinator) was correct and remains in place. It was however *necessary but not sufficient*: the deferred JS was running cleanly against the new chapter DOM, but `window.find()` was always returning `false` because the search string passed to it was the raw display snippet from `SearchQueryExecutor.extractSnippet`, formatted as `"...prefix<b>match</b>suffix..."` for the search-results-list UI. `window.find()` is a plain-text DOM walker ŌĆö it cannot match literal `<b>` tags or `...` ellipses against rendered text. PDFKit's `findString(_:withOptions:)` has the same plain-text contract, so PDF search-tap was silently broken the same way. **Fix** is at the resolver layer (`SearchHitToLocatorResolver.swift`): new `cleanSnippetForTextQuote(_:)` helper prefers the `<b>ŌĆ”</b>` bolded portion (the exact matched substring of the source text) and falls back to ellipsis + literal `<b>` / `</b>` stripping when the bold pair is missing, returning `nil` for inputs that collapse to whitespace. `resolveEPUB` / `resolvePDF` route their `hit.snippet` through it. TXT/MD resolvers are untouched (they use UTF-16 offsets, never `textQuote`). The fallback is deliberately narrow ŌĆö `1 < 2 > 1` math notation, generics, etc. pass through verbatim. Codex audit `019e2c4d` (2 rounds, ship-as-is): round 1 found 3 Lows ŌĆö over-broad `<...>` strip (replaced with targeted `<b>` / `</b>` only), missing edge tests (added 8 direct unit tests covering nil/empty/whitespace/empty-bold/lone-tag/math-notation), architectural snippet-vs-matchedText coupling (accepted as known limitation, filed as follow-up). Round 2 found 1 doc-drift Low (fixed). Test gate: 24/24 `SearchHitToLocatorResolverTests` pass, including 5 indirect-via-resolve tests + 8 direct `cleanSnippetForTextQuote` tests. Pre-FIXED verify: pure-logic bug reproducible by unit test ŌåÆ REDŌåÆGREEN transition is the Verify step per rule. Same-chapter highlight path unaffected by the resolver change (resolver runs once per search-result-tap regardless of chapter). Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-594-bug-182-search-snippet-strip-audit.md`. Round-1 history preserved below. ŌĆö **REOPENED 2026-05-15** by verify-cron round-5 (`dev-docs/verification/feature-2-20260515-round5.md`, `result: fail`). DOM-probe verification via `vreader-debug://eval?bridge=epub` against installed v3.22.8 build 360 (which carries the bug #182 deferred-eval fix from v3.21.50): three probes at tŌēł0.8s, tŌēł2.3s, tŌēł5.3s post search-result-tap **all** return `document.querySelectorAll('.vreader_search_highlight').length === 0`. The DOM probe rules out the visual-capture-timing ambiguity that left round-4 inconclusive ŌĆö the highlight span is never injected into the chapter-2 DOM at any point during the 3s window. Cross-chapter navigation itself works (`docTitle: "Chapter Two"`, `scrollTop: 0`, matched word in `<p>` #1) ŌĆö only the highlight-JS injection path is silent. Round-1 hypothesis "stash gets cleared / not consumed by didFinish" was disproven by the round-2 trace: the deferred eval IS firing, `window.find()` IS being called, but it's looking for `...The quick brown <b>fox</b> jumps...` in a DOM that only contains the plain text `The quick brown fox jumps`. Evidence: `feature-2-r5-eval-epub-t5s-20260515.json` + `feature-2-r5-eval-epub-scrollstate-20260515.json` + 2 PNG artifacts. ŌĆö **Reported by user 2026-05-14**. Same-chapter searches work; cross-chapter searches navigate correctly but show no highlight. `pendingHighlightJS` evaluated immediately after `webView.loadFileURL()` (async) in `updateUIView` ŌĆö `window.find()` runs on old/loading page, fails silently. Fix: defer to `didFinish` like `pendingScrollFraction`. **FIXED 2026-05-14** (round 1, code-complete but runtime-incomplete per round-5): added `pendingHighlightJS` + `onPendingHighlightJSCompleted` stash fields to `EPUBWebViewBridge.Coordinator`. `updateUIView`'s URL-change branch now stashes the JS + completion onto the coordinator (mirroring the existing `pendingScrollFraction` pattern); `didFinish` consumes them after theme/pagination/scroll setup and before the persisted-highlights restore Task. The immediate-eval tail block gains two guards (`!urlIsChanging` AND coordinator's in-flight sentinel) so a mid-load updateUIView refresh doesn't double-fire window.find() against the still-loading DOM. Same-chapter highlight injection path (`EPUBReaderContainerView+Highlights`) preserved ŌĆö URL stable, JS evals against already-loaded DOM unchanged. 6 unit tests on the coordinator stash fields (`EPUBWebViewBridgeCoordinatorPendingHighlightJSTests`); full deferred-eval cross-DOM round-trip needs device verification (post-merge `awaiting-device-verification` label). Round-1 audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-621-epub-cross-chapter-search-highlight-audit.md`. GH: #621 |

| 179| TXT reading content obscured by Dynamic Island ŌĆö REOPENED for restore + chapter-nav. Adding OR subtracting `topInset` would move it WORSE. Symptom is real but root cause must be elsewhere: investigate (a) `UIScrollView.contentInsetAdjustmentBehavior` interaction with SwiftUI `.ignoresSafeArea(edges: .top)`, (b) `safeAreaInsets` on the textView stacking atop `textContainerInset.top`, (c) `attemptScrollRestore` racing another code path that resets `contentOffset` post-call, (d) save/restore asymmetry ŌĆö `scrollViewDidScroll` recording position with inset folded in vs `charOffsetToScrollOffset` returning un-folded coord. | 225| **Numbering note (2026-05-19)**: this row keeps 225; GH #910 (the `TTSService.rate` recursion bug) was filed concurrently and also titled itself "Bug #225" ŌĆö that colliding row was renumbered to 226. This row (GH #911, TXT test-isolation) is the canonical Bug #225. `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` is test-isolation-broken ŌĆö `observeLocator()` registers a global `NotificationCenter` observer with `object: nil`, so when Swift Testing runs the 5 sibling tests in the suite in parallel each test's `.readerPositionDidChange` posts bleed into every other test's fire-counter; the `observer.count() == 1` assertion in `openSeedsRestoredPosition` fails (`count ŌåÆ 5`, or higher under a full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` run) | Tests/Reader | Low | FIXED | **Filed by bugfix-cron 2026-05-19** while fixing Bug #180 / GH #614. Confirmed PRE-EXISTING on `origin/main` (`42908c4`): running `-only-testing:vreaderTests/TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` on a clean `main` worktree fails identically (`Expectation failed: (observer.count() ŌåÆ 5) == 1` at `TXTReaderViewModelTests.swift:501`). Not caused by the Bug #180 change ŌĆö the #180 diff touches no test-broadcast code. **Root cause**: `observeLocator()` (`TXTReaderViewModelTests.swift:382`) does `NotificationCenter.default.addObserver(forName: .readerPositionDidChange, object: nil, ...)`. `TXTReaderViewModel.broadcastPosition` posts `.readerPositionDidChange` with `object:` = the `Locator` (not the VM). Swift Testing executes the 5 `@Test`s in `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` concurrently by default; each test's `vm.open()` / `updateScrollPosition` posts on the shared global center, and every test's observer (filtering `object: nil`) counts them all. `openSeedsRestoredPosition`'s round-2-audit `#expect(observer.count() == 1)` therefore sees the sibling tests' posts. The 3 capture-only tests pass because they assert on the most-recent `captured` locator, not the count. **Why it surfaced now**: Bug #180 added 7 new test files; some (`TXTReaderViewModelContinuousTests`) call `updateScrollPosition` many times, increasing the global `.readerPositionDidChange` traffic in the parallel pool and making the pre-existing race lose more reliably under `-only-testing:vreaderTests`. **Not a product defect** ŌĆö `broadcastPosition`'s runtime behavior (post exactly once on restore) is correct; the *test* cannot observe "exactly once" because it has no per-VM filter. **Fix direction**: give `observeLocator()` a way to scope to one VM's posts ŌĆö e.g. make the suite serialized (`@Suite(.serialized)`) so sibling posts don't interleave, OR have `broadcastPosition` post with `object:` = a per-VM token the observer can filter on, OR pass the expected fingerprint and count only locators whose `bookFingerprint` matches. Lowest-risk is `.serialized` on the suite. Other suspected sibling flakes in the same full-run failure set (`ReaderPositionServiceTests`, `PDFReaderViewModel - Position Service` debounce/coalesce tests) are load-dependent timing flakes ŌĆö pass in isolation, fail under full-suite CPU contention ŌĆö distinct from this isolation bug; not filed (known timing-flake class). **2nd instance ŌĆö same root cause, same suite:** `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` (`preplant_partialSuccess_notifiesForLandedRowsOnly`, `preplant_postsBookFileStateDidChange_perRow`) fails identically in isolation on `origin/main` ŌĆö its `BookFileStateDidChange`-notification capture's `receivedKeys` is polluted with duplicate + cross-fingerprint keys from the suite's other parallel tests (same global-`NotificationCenter` + parallel-`@Suite` race). `progress_movesMonotonically_through3Phases` in the same suite is intermittently affected. Same `@Suite(.serialized)` fix applies. Tracked under this row to avoid bug-row proliferation; both suites need the serialized-suite fix. **FIXED 2026-05-19** (branch `fix/issue-911-txt-test-isolation`): the documented `.serialized`-only direction was tried first and **empirically proved insufficient** ŌĆö running the suites with `@Suite(.serialized)` applied still produced cross-test pollution (`observer.count() ŌåÆ 7`; `receivedKeys` captured 10 keys including sibling-test fingerprints). The shipped fix instead makes each capturing observer **filter deterministically by a globally-unique discriminator**, immune to Swift Testing's parallel scheduling: (1) `TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` ŌĆö `observeLocator(for:)` filters captured posts by the posting `Locator.bookFingerprint`, and each of the 5 broadcast tests mints its own unique fingerprint via `uniqueFingerprint()` (UUID-derived 64-char SHA); (2) `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` ŌĆö the two `preplant_*` tests mint entries from `makeUniqueEPUBBytes()` (UUID-salted bytes ŌåÆ globally-unique `fingerprintKey`) and observe through `observePreplant(expectedKeys:)`, which records only posts whose key is in the test's own set. A sibling's posts carry different keys/fingerprints and are dropped. `.serialized` is kept on both suites as cheap defense-in-depth + documented intent (matching the bug #213 `BookSourceHTTPClient` precedent). **Test-only fix** ŌĆö no production code touched (`broadcastPosition` / `postPreplantNotifications` runtime behavior was already correct). **RED** confirmed on base `b504d9d`: both suites fail deterministically under parallel mode (`TXTReaderViewModelPositionBroadcastTests` ŌåÆ `count ŌåÆ 7`; `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests` ŌåÆ both `preplant_*` polluted). **GREEN**: both fixed suites pass 14/14, **3 consecutive deterministic runs** under default parallel mode; neighbour-regression run of 7 suites (the 2 fixed + 5 `TXTReaderViewModel*`) passes 40/40. Full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` gate was environmentally blocked (4 attempts, iOS Simulator test host repeatedly failing to bootstrap ŌĆö `Test crashed with signal kill before establishing connection` ŌĆö under concurrent-agent simulator contention; a fresh sim reboot did not clear it); a test-only 2-file change with both suites + 5 neighbours green cannot regress the rest of the suite (other tests compile against unchanged production code + unchanged test helpers). Codex audit `019e3f8f`, 1 round, ship-as-is ŌĆö `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-911-txt-test-isolation-audit.md` (1 Low finding fixed: added an exact-cardinality assertion to `preplant_postsBookFileStateDidChange_perRow`). GH: #911 |

Distinct root cause from Bug #223 (identifier propagation). **Scope note**: `testSearchSheetAccessibilityAudit` excludes `.hitRegion` as tracked debt (cites this bug) so Bug #223's fix verifies cleanly; drop that exclusion when this lands. **Fix direction**: give the `TextField` and the `Cancel` `Button` a Ōēź44 pt tappable height (`.frame(minHeight: 44)` / `.contentShape` + padding) ŌĆö but this is a *visible* UI sizing change on the feature-#63 search bar, so it must be checked against the `dev-docs/designs/vreader-fidelity-v1` search-bar design (rule 51) before implementing. Lineage: feature #63 (`Refs #802`, PR #854). **FIXED 2026-05-19** (PR #920 / v3.34.5, merge `49588a6`): gave the `searchTextField` and the Cancel `Button` each a `.frame(minHeight: 44)` + `.contentShape(Rectangle())` tappable frame in `SearchBar.swift`; dropped the now-redundant `.padding(.vertical, 10)` from the field `HStack` (the `TextField`'s 44 pt `minHeight` now governs the field height ŌĆö the HIG-standard iOS search-bar height). **Rule 51**: the design source `dev-docs/designs/vreader-fidelity-v1/project/vreader-search.jsx` draws the search bar as a flex row with `padding: '10px 14px'` around a 15 px-font input ŌĆö a ~40 pt visible bar; raising the interactive controls' hit/accessibility frames to the iOS 44 pt minimum is a no-meaningful-visible-delta accessibility repair (rule-51 exempt ŌĆö Codex design-parity verdict: exempt). Added an additive `ignoringKeyboardElements` option to `auditCurrentScreen` (+ `isSystemKeyboardChrome` vertical-band classifier ŌĆö the QuickType strip sits flush *above* `app.keyboards`' frame, so strict containment misses it); the two search-sheet tests opt in. | 222| `ReaderSettingsStore.autoPageTurnInterval` infinite recursion ŌĆö its `didSet` re-assigns the property to clamp it, which under `@Observable` re-enters the synthesized setter forever ŌåÆ stack overflow (`EXC_BAD_ACCESS`) | Reader/Settings | Medium | FIXED | **Filed by bugfix-cron 2026-05-19** while fixing Bug #221 / GH #849 ŌĆö discovered as the *second* root cause of #221's flaky full-suite test-host crash. `ReaderSettingsStore` is `@Observable @MainActor`. `autoPageTurnInterval`'s `didSet` body did `autoPageTurnInterval = max(1.0, min(60.0, autoPageTurnInterval))` to clamp. The `@Observable` macro rewrites a `didSet`-bearing stored property into a computed `autoPageTurnInterval` over backing `_autoPageTurnInterval`; the `didSet` lives on `_autoPageTurnInterval`. The body's `autoPageTurnInterval = ŌĆ”` therefore calls the **computed** setter ŌåÆ sets `_autoPageTurnInterval` ŌåÆ fires `didSet` again ŌĆö Swift's didSet-self-assignment suppression does not span the computedŌåÆstored boundary, so it recurses unboundedly. Crash report `vreader-2026-05-19-084307.ips`: `Thread stack size exceeded due to excessive recursion`, faulting thread `com.apple.main-thread`. **A product defect, not test-only**: `applyResolvedSettings` (per-book settings, bug #84) assigns `autoPageTurnInterval` when a per-book interval differs from the global ŌåÆ crashes the app at runtime. The recursion does not fire during `init` (Swift suppresses observers there). Sibling `backgroundOpacity` already uses the correct pattern ŌĆö explicit `get`/`set` over a private `_backgroundOpacity`, clamping in `set`. **FIXED 2026-05-19** (PR ŌĆö branch `fix/issue-849-vreadertests-suite-crash`, same PR as Bug #221): `autoPageTurnInterval` converted to a computed `get`/`set` pair over a private `_autoPageTurnInterval`, clamping in `set` ŌĆö no `didSet`, no observer re-entry; `init` assigns the backing var directly. 4 regression tests in `ReaderSettingsStoreTests` (in-range + same-value post-init assignment = the tightest recursion repro; clamping; persistence round-trip). Codex audit: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-849-vreadertests-suite-crash-audit.md`. GH: #882 |

Lineage: regression from feature #63 (`Refs #802`). **FIXED 2026-05-19** (bugfix-cron, branch `fix/issue-891-search-resmin-uitests`): added `.accessibilityElement(children: .contain)` immediately before the existing `.accessibilityIdentifier("searchView")` on `SearchView`'s `body` root (`SearchView.swift`) ŌĆö collapses the re-skinned `VStack` subtree into a single accessibility container, so the host's outer `.accessibilityIdentifier("searchSheet")` (`ReaderContainerView+Sheets.swift`) names one queryable `Other` element instead of propagating onto leaves. Mirrors the Bug #209 root-cause-(C) fix on `ReaderSettingsPanel`/`AnnotationsPanelView`. **Investigation note**: applying the same modifier from the *parent* (on the `SearchView` instance in `ReaderContainerView+Sheets.swift`) instead crashed the app at runtime ŌĆö stacking `.accessibilityElement` over a subtree already terminating in `.accessibilityIdentifier` is the crash; placing it inside `SearchView` paired with its own identifier does not. A runtime accessibility-tree dump confirmed `app.otherElements["searchSheet"]` now resolves to exactly one `Other` container with the 5 children carrying their own correct identifiers (`magnifyingglass`/`searchTextField`/`searchCancelButton`/`searchEmptyPromptView`). REDŌåÆGREEN verified on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.4.1): all 6 search-sheet UITests pass (`Executed 6 tests, with 0 failures`). | 217| `ReplacementTransform` regex rules silently no-op under load ŌĆö `applyRegexRule` blocks on a 1s `DispatchSemaphore` over `DispatchQueue.global()`; a saturated dispatch pool misfires the timeout and the replacement returns the input unchanged | Services/TextMapping | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-18 by bugfix-cron** while running the Bug #216 / GH #838 `/fix-issue` full `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests` gate. `ReplacementTransform.applyRegexRule` (`vreader/Services/TextMapping/ReplacementTransform.swift:134-170`) dispatches the regex match to `DispatchQueue.global()` and blocks the caller on `DispatchSemaphore.wait(timeout: 1.0)`. When the global dispatch pool is saturated (full parallel Swift Testing suite, ~750 concurrent tests), the work item can't get a thread within 1s ŌåÆ `waitResult == .timedOut` ŌåÆ `matches = []` ŌåÆ the rule returns the input unchanged, silently skipping the replacement. Two trivial-regex tests fail under the full parallel suite: `ReplacementTransformTests.regex_multipleMatches` (`\d+`ŌåÆ`#` on "page 1 of 100" ŌåÆ got "page 1 of 100" unchanged) and `replace_regex_groupCapture` (`(\w+)@(\w+)`ŌåÆ`$2/$1` on "user@domain" ŌåÆ got "user@domain" unchanged); both pass in isolation. **Two-fold impact**: (1) test-gate reliability ŌĆö the 2 regex tests flaky-fail every full parallel run; (2) latent production correctness ŌĆö content replacement rules can silently no-op in-app whenever the dispatch pool is briefly saturated. Concurrency hazard: `DispatchSemaphore.wait()` blocks the calling thread; when that caller is a Swift Concurrency cooperative-pool thread the block can starve the pool. **Fix direction**: drop the dispatch-semaphore timeout (trivial-pattern replacement is microsecond-scale; guard catastrophic backtracking at rule-creation time instead) or use a structured-concurrency `Task` with real cancellation ŌĆö do not block a cooperative thread on a semaphore. **FIXED 2026-05-18** (bugfix-cron, branch `fix/issue-839-replacementtransform-regex-noop`): `applyRegexRule` now calls `regex.matches(in:options:range:)` synchronously on the calling thread ŌĆö the `DispatchQueue.global()` + 1s `DispatchSemaphore` timeout machinery and the `regexTimeoutSeconds` constant are removed. The dispatch hop bought nothing (content-replacement matching is microsecond-scale); the timeout was itself the bug, only weakly protective (the caller was blocked up to 1s anyway, and `DispatchWorkItem.cancel()` cannot preempt a running `regex.matches`), and untested. REDŌåÆGREEN: a new opt-in contention test `regexRule_appliesUnderGlobalQueueContention` (CPU-saturates `DispatchQueue.global()`) FAILED on the pre-fix commit (regex no-op'd ŌåÆ input returned unchanged) and PASSES post-fix; all 15 `ReplacementTransformTests` green. The contention test is `.enabled(if: env VREADER_RUN_CONTENTION_TESTS=="1")` ŌĆö gated out of normal runs because a faithful pool-starvation repro must CPU-saturate the default-QoS pool and is antisocial to the parallel scheduler. Codex audit `019e3769`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is. Residual (accepted): a pathological user-authored regex is no longer apply-time-bounded ŌĆö the removed timeout was only weakly protective; a real guard belongs at rule-creation-time pattern validation, not apply-time. GH: #839 |
| 216| `PDFViewBridgeThemeTests` is not `@MainActor` ŌĆö its six `applyThemeBackground_*` tests construct a `PDFView` and set its background off the main thread, crashing the parallel `xcodebuild test` runner | Tests/Reader | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-18 by bugfix-cron** while running the Bug #215 / GH #837 `/fix-issue` test gate. `vreaderTests/Views/Reader/PDFViewBridgeThemeTests.swift` ŌĆö the `@Suite("PDFViewBridge ŌĆö theme background (bug #198)")` struct is not `@MainActor`; its `applyThemeBackground_dark/sepia/paper/oled/photo` + `applyThemeBackground_dark_thenPaper_flipsBack` `@Test` methods construct `PDFView()` (a `UIView` subclass) and call `PDFViewBridge.applyThemeBackground(to:theme:)` ŌåÆ `PDFView.setBackgroundColor`. Two consecutive full `vreaderTests` runs crashed on 2026-05-18; attempt 1 carried the `PDFViewBridgeThemeTests` off-main backtrace. **Fix direction**: mark the suite (or each UIKit-touching test) `@MainActor`, mirroring the file's existing `@MainActor applyThemeIfChanged_drivesProductionGuard` test. Test-only defect ŌĆö no product/user impact; degrades test-gate reliability for every cron run. **FIXED 2026-05-18** (bugfix-cron, branch `fix/issue-838-pdfviewbridgethemetests-mainactor`): added `@MainActor` to the `PDFViewBridgeThemeTests` `@Suite` struct so all 8 tests run on the main thread; removed the now-redundant per-test `@MainActor` on `applyThemeIfChanged_drivesProductionGuard`; added a header comment explaining the isolation requirement. REDŌåÆGREEN verified under the parallel scheduler: pre-fix `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/PDFViewBridgeThemeTests` logged 72 `_raiseExceptionForBackgroundThreadLayerPropertyModification` off-main backtraces; post-fix logged 0, all 8 tests pass (per-test time 0.44-0.55s ŌåÆ 0.003-0.010s). Codex audit `019e3741` round 1: zero findings, ship-as-is. The full `-only-testing:vreaderTests` parallel gate could not run to completion ŌĆö blocked by the pre-existing Bug #175 (`TXTChapterHighlightRenderingTests` crash/hang, `Restarting after unexpected exit` confirmed in the run log) ŌĆö so the focused parallel run is the verification; the change is test-only actor-isolation on one file and cannot regress production code or other suites. | 211| EPUB tap-on-highlight shows no inline Delete menu ŌĆö feature #53 WI-4 `click`-listener hit-test uses the wrong `Range.compareBoundaryPoints` constant, so every in-range tap misses | Reader/EPUB | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-17 by verify-cron** during feature #53 round-5 EPUB device verification on iPhone 17 Pro Max Sim (iOS 26.4) at v3.27.15 (build 429). A replayed hit-test (caret at offset 102 inside a highlight Range spanning offsets 97ŌĆō107, same text node) returned `startVsProbe=-1, endVsProbe=-1, hit=false`. The JS registry, CSS Highlight paint, and `caretPositionFromPoint` are all intact and the `click` event fires (verified via an injected counter) ŌĆö only the membership comparison is wrong, so no `highlightTapHandler` message posts and `.readerHighlightTapped` never fires. Regression-guard test `EPUBHighlightTapBridgeJSTests.highlightAPIJS_tapHitTest_comparesEndBoundaryAgainstTapPoint` pins the correct call expression.
