| 205| UIEditMenuInteraction logs Error on `presentEditMenu(with:)` ŌĆö TXT tap-on-highlight menu still invisible after Bug #203 coord-space fix shipped (likely UITextView own-edit-menu conflict OR add+present timing) | Reader/TXT, Reader/* | Medium | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-17** in branch `fix/issue-751-uieditmenuinteraction-weak-delegate` (PR pending). Both verify-cron root-cause hypotheses (UITextView own-edit-menu conflict; add+present timing) were wrong. Real root cause confirmed from the iOS 26.5 SDK header: `UIEditMenuInteraction` declares `delegate` as a **weak** property (`@property (nonatomic, weak, nullable, readonly) id<UIEditMenuInteractionDelegate> delegate;`). `UIKitHighlightActionPresenter.present` created its `PresenterDelegate` as a local with no owning reference, so the delegate deallocated the instant `present` returned; UIKit then asynchronously composed the menu, queried a now-nil delegate, found no menu, and logged `<compose failure>`. **Fix**: the delegate is associated onto the `UIEditMenuInteraction` object itself (`objc_setAssociatedObject`, `OBJC_ASSOCIATION_RETAIN_NONATOMIC`) ŌĆö the interaction, strongly retained by the host view, owns its delegate, so the delegate lives exactly as long as the interaction. This binds the lifetime to the interaction rather than the presenter, which matters because the reader containers build `UIKitHighlightActionPresenter()` inline in `body` and `TXTTextViewBridge.updateUIView` rebinds it on every SwiftUI render (an earlier presenter-holds-delegate fix would have been a flaky race ŌĆö caught by the Codex audit). `present` also sweeps any prior presenter-installed edit-menu interaction off the view (keyed on the association, so the text view's own built-in menu is untouched). REDŌåÆGREEN: 4 tests in `UIKitHighlightActionPresenterTests` ŌĆö `interaction.delegate` reads non-nil after `present` (the weak property proves retention), interaction installed on the host view, two `present` calls supersede rather than accumulate, unrelated edit-menu interactions survive the sweep. Codex audit `019e345b`, 3 rounds, ship-as-is ŌĆö round 1 caught the ephemeral-presenter race (High) + weak test seam, round 2 caught the abort-path linger (Medium) + a comment-policy-name Low, round 3 clean. Audit log: `.claude/codex-audits/fix-issue-751-uieditmenuinteraction-weak-delegate-audit.md`. **Filed by verify-cron 2026-05-16** during Bug #203 / Feature #53 round-3 device verification on iPhone 17 Pro Sim (iOS 26.5) at v3.23.9 (commit cfab8c5, build 386 ŌĆö fresh post-WI-1 install). Repro: `vreader-debug://reset` ŌåÆ seed war-and-peace ŌåÆ tap card ŌåÆ reader opens at chapter 1 page 2/4 ŌåÆ long-press "Prince" ŌåÆ custom menu (Highlight/Add Note/Define/Ō¢Č) ŌåÆ tap Highlight ŌåÆ "Prince" yellow + `snapshot.highlightCount: 1` Ō£ō ŌåÆ dismiss selection via neutral tap (chrome toggles off, consistent) ŌåÆ tap on yellow "Prince" ŌåÆ **NO inline edit/delete menu**. Bug #202 chrome-toggle suppression IS active (tap-on-highlight short-circuits before chrome-toggle fall-through). Bug #203 coord-space fix shipped (sourceRect is now textView-local). But the menu still doesn't appear. **Evidence**: iOS log subsystem `[com.apple.UIKit:EditMenuInteraction]` reports `Error`-level events correlated with each tap-on-yellow attempt (06:37:06.411 + 06:37:35.673 from `xcrun simctl spawn booted log show --predicate 'process == "vreader"'`). Message body privacy-redacted (`<compose failure [shared UUID]>`) but severity + subsystem confirm UIKit is rejecting the `presentEditMenu(with:)` call. **Suspect root cause** (code-read at `HighlightActionPresenter.swift:118-124`): (a) UITextView already owns a built-in `UIEditMenuInteraction` for its selection menu; for the TXT non-chunked path the `view` passed to `present(for:in:)` IS the HighlightableTextView, and adding a SECOND UIEditMenuInteraction to a UITextView may conflict with the system one. (b) Synchronous `view.addInteraction(interaction)` + `interaction.presentEditMenu(with: cfg)` in the same call may not give UIKit a runloop tick to integrate the interaction into the responder chain ŌĆö Apple sample code sometimes dispatches present to next main-queue cycle. **Fix direction**: prefer (a) ŌĆö pass `textView.superview` or a reader-container view to `present(for:in:)` so the menu hosts on a view without an existing UIEditMenuInteraction; the sourceRect (already textView-local) gets converted to the host's coord space same shape as the chunked path's existing wrapper. (b) as cheaper backup if (a) doesn't address it. **Affects**: Feature #53 acceptance criterion (a) for TXT ŌĆö round-3 device verify is `partial`. Likely also MD (same TXT bridge), EPUB (webView host ŌĆö may NOT have the conflict, needs verification), PDF (pdfView host ŌĆö same question). Foliate uses `.zero` sourceRect, separately tracked. Bug #203 close-gate verify is now `partial`/`fail` for this distinct second issue. GH: #751 |

| 227| `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests.case11b` fails deterministically ŌĆö `awaitReaderSettled` throws `.settleTimeout` immediately on a same-key reopen | DevTools/* | Medium | FIXED | **Filed 2026-05-19 by the feature #55 (tap-on-annotated-text note preview) implementation run** during the WI-5 full-suite test gate. `case11b_sameKeyReopen_oldUnregisterCancelsOnlyOwnWaiter()` fails **deterministically** ŌĆö 3/3 isolated runs of the `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests` suite ŌĆö and fails **fast** (~0.06s, far under the test's 2.0s timeout budget), so `registry.awaitReaderSettled(for:token:timeout:2.0)` is throwing `DebugReaderProbeError.settleTimeout` *immediately* rather than resolving when probe B's `markReaderSettled` fires. **Repro**: `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests/DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests` on iPhone 17 Pro Sim ŌĆö `case11b` records an issue at `DebugReaderRegistrySettleCleanupTests.swift:169` (`Caught error: .settleTimeout`); the suite's other 5 tests pass. **Analysis**: the test registers probe A (token A) then probe B (token B) on the same key, spawns a `Task` that unregisters A at +50ms then `markReaderSettled(token: B)` at +100ms, and `await`s `awaitReaderSettled(token: B, timeout: 2.0)`. The three settle suites (`DebugReaderRegistrySettle{Core,EdgeCase,Cleanup}Tests`) all drove the `DebugReaderRegistry.shared` **singleton** via `shared.reset()`. Swift Testing runs `@Test` methods in parallel; `case11b` keeps a `settleWaiter` suspended ~100ms (background `Task` unregisters A at +50ms, marks B settled at +100ms). During that window a *concurrent* test's `shared.reset()` wipes `settleWaiters` and resumes `case11b`'s waiter with a spurious `.settleTimeout`. The issue's two hypotheses are both wrong ŌĆö the production `awaitReaderSettled`/`markReaderSettled`/`clearSettleState`/`unregister` same-key-reopen bookkeeping is correct (confirmed: `-parallel-testing-enabled NO` ŌåÆ all 6 cleanup tests pass; the "3/3 isolated runs" used a suite-level filter that still parallelizes all 6 methods). **Fix**: added DEBUG-only `DebugReaderRegistry.makeIsolatedForTests()` factory; the three settle suites' `makeRegistry()` now construct a fresh isolated instance per test ŌĆö no shared mutable state, deterministic under parallelism. **Verified**: 3 settle suites (17 tests) pass 3/3 in parallel; `case11b` resolves in ~0.10s via B's mark. The panel swipe-delete (`HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight`) posts `.readerHighlightRemoved`, whose object is only the highlight **UUID string** ŌĆö no CFI ŌĆö and the Foliate Coordinator does not observe `.readerHighlightRemoved`. `removeHighlight` also deletes the `HighlightRecord` from persistence *before* posting, so a post-hoc `fetchHighlights` cannot recover the deleted record's CFI. The Foliate restore path (`FoliateSpikeView+Restore.swift`) only *adds* annotations (idempotent) and never reconciles removals. **Pre-existing latent gap** ŌĆö the panel-delete path never posted `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete`, even before #55 ŌĆö **surfaced by feature #55 WI-7**, which re-homed the AZW3/MOBI highlight tap to the #55 note preview and dropped the legacy #53 tap-time delete menu (`FoliateHighlightTapHandlerModifier.performDelete`, the only former producer of `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete`). After WI-7 the panel is the only delete path for AZW3/MOBI highlights, so the gap is now user-observable on the only supported path. EPUB is unaffected ŌĆö `EPUBReaderContainerView` observes `.readerHighlightRemoved` and strips its WKWebView highlight via `HighlightCoordinator.handleRemoval` / `EPUBHighlightBridge.removeHighlightJS`. **Repro**: open an AZW3/MOBI book, create a highlight, swipe-delete it in the Annotations panel Highlights tab ŌåÆ highlight gone from the panel list but its colored overlay still painted in the reader; close+reopen the book ŌåÆ overlay now gone. **Fix direction**: plumb the CFI to the Foliate strip on a panel-delete ŌĆö either (a) `HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight` captures the record's `.epub` anchor CFI before the persistence delete and posts `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` (cfi + fingerprintKey) alongside `.readerHighlightRemoved` (reuses the existing dormant Foliate observer ŌĆö kept intentionally post-WI-7 as this hook), or (b) the Foliate host maintains a `[UUID: CFI]` cache populated as highlights restore/create and consults it on `.readerHighlightRemoved`. (a) is smaller but touches shared #53 highlight infrastructure; (b) keeps the change Foliate-local. **Severity Medium** ŌĆö AZW3/MOBI-only, a stale visual that self-corrects on reload; persistence is correct, no data loss. **FIXED 2026-05-20** (branch `fix/issue-938-foliate-panel-delete-overlay-strip`): applied fix-direction (a) ŌĆö `HighlightListViewModel.removeHighlight` now captures the pre-delete record from `self.highlights` (the authoritative in-memory copy after `loadHighlights`), extracts the `.epub` anchor CFI via a new `private static epubAnchorCFI(of:)` helper that mirrors `FoliateHighlightJSBridge.cfi(from:)` (treats `nil` record, `nil` / non-`.epub` / empty-CFI anchor as no-CFI), and posts `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` with `["cfi": String, "fingerprintKey": String]` userInfo alongside the existing `.readerHighlightRemoved` (UUID). **Emission order** mirrors `FoliateHighlightJSBridge.delete` ŌĆö `.readerHighlightRemoved` first (panel/list sync), then `.foliateRequestAnnotationJSDelete` (SVG overlay strip); a regression test pins this order. **Atomicity**: a persistence-delete throw posts neither notification ŌĆö guarantees the overlay never strips a still-persisted highlight. **RED**: new `HighlightListViewModelFoliateOverlayStripTests` 6-test suite covered the epub-anchored happy path (with strict ordering assertion), pre-delete CFI capture, `.text`-anchor skip, nil-anchor skip, empty-CFI skip, and persistence-failure atomicity ŌĆö failed 4├Ś on pre-fix RED, passed 6/6 post-GREEN. **Verified GREEN**: focused suite 6/6, full `xcodebuild test -only-testing:vreaderTests` 6811/6811 in 35.6s, deterministic. | 230| `SelectiveRestoreCoordinatorTests.progress_movesMonotonically_through3Phases` is a flaky test ŌĆö `#expect(values.last == 1.0)` intermittently fails with `values.last ŌåÆ 0.85` under CPU load | Tests/Backup | Low | FIXED | **FIXED 2026-05-21 in v3.38.40** ŌĆö replaced the detached-`Task`-per-callback recorder + `Task.yield()` drain with a synchronous lock-guarded `final class Collector: @unchecked Sendable`. The `progress` param is `@Sendable (Double) -> Void` called synchronously by the coordinator, so recording inline (`progress: { v in collector.record(v) }`) guarantees every value is captured in call order by the time `restoreSelectively` returns ŌĆö no detached Task, no `Task.yield()` race. Verified deterministic: 5/5 consecutive isolated runs green. Test-only change; production progress reporting untouched. **Filed 2026-05-19 by the Bug #225 / GH #911 `/fix-issue` run** during post-merge close-gate verification (observed once on merged `origin/main` commit `ad66db1`, in a combined 2-suite run; passes 3/3 in isolation-suite runs). **Separate defect from Bug #225** ŌĆö does NOT involve `NotificationCenter` cross-test pollution at all, so it was out of #225's scope and is filed separately per the working agreement (discover-a-bug ŌåÆ file, don't fix in an unrelated PR). The test then does `await Task.yield()` twice and reads `await collector.values`. `Task.yield()` is not a synchronization primitive ŌĆö it does not guarantee previously-spawned detached `Task`s have run; under load the final callback's `Task` (recording `1.0`) has not executed when the test reads `values`, so `values.last` is the penultimate value `0.85`. **Fix direction**: make the test deterministically await all progress callbacks before asserting ŌĆö collect progress values synchronously in the closure (no detached `Task`), OR make `restoreSelectively`'s `progress` closure `async` and `await`-ed so the final callback completes before the call returns. This is exactly `.claude/rules/10-tdd.md`'s documented anti-pattern ("Bare `Task.sleep(...)` for sync ŌåÆ flaky in CI ŌåÆ use `XCTestExpectation` with timeout"). `BackgroundIndexingCoordinatorTests`' 10 intermittent failures (`status ŌåÆ .indexing` instead of `.indexed`, `count ŌåÆ 0`) are the same class ŌĆö async work unfinished at assert time under load. **Repro**: run the full `vreaderTests` suite while other simulator-bound work runs concurrently; `speakCompletesWithDidFinish` fails ~50ŌĆō100% of the time; in isolation it passes. **Fix direction**: replace the bare `Task.sleep`-then-assert with a deterministic wait on the actual completion signal ŌĆö an `XCTestExpectation` fulfilled by the `RecordingDelegate`'s `didFinish` callback with a generous `fulfillment(of:timeout:)`, OR have the mock expose an `async` "timeline finished" awaitable the test can `await` directly. | 286| Tapping a chapter in the TXT TOC navigates to the wrong chapter/position (distinct from FIXED #234 ŌĆö different root cause). | vreader/Views/Reader/ReaderTOCBuilder.swift, vreader/Services/TXT/TXTService.swift | Medium | FIXED | **Root cause**: TXT TOC offsets and the reader's chapter index came from TWO independent chapter-detection passes that could disagree. The TOC pass (`ReaderTOCFactory.buildTOC` case "txt") decoded via `TXTService.detectEncodingFromSample` + raw `String(data:encoding:)` with a UTF-8-only fallback, then ran its OWN `TXTTocRuleEngine.detectBestRule` over that string (`TOCBuilder.forTXT`). The reader pass (`TXTService.openChapterBased`) decodes via `decodeForDisplayAndSearch` (full GBK/Big5/NSString-heuristic ladder), runs `detectBestRule` over the full decoded string, then `buildChapterIndexFromFullText`. On non-UTF-8 files ŌĆö or files whose 8KB encoding sample misdetects (e.g. an ASCII head followed by a GBK body) ŌĆö the two decoded strings differ, so every UTF-16 offset shifts and the Nth TOC entry's offset ŌēĀ the Nth reader-chapter start. In **Paged** layout `navigateToGlobalOffset` floor-snaps (`ch.globalStartUTF16 <= globalUTF16`), amplifying the disagreement to a whole wrong chapter; in **Scroll** the scroll pos is right but the displayed chapter is wrong. The comments at `ReaderTOCBuilder.swift` / `TXTService.swift` asserted "TOC and chapters are perfectly aligned" ŌĆö FALSE, because the TOC path was never converted to the reader's full-decode pipeline. **Fix (single source of truth)**: new `TXTService.buildTXTTOCEntries(data:fingerprint:)` decodes via `decodeForDisplayAndSearch` (= reader), runs the same `detectBestRule`, calls the same `buildChapterIndexFromFullText`, and maps each chapter to a `TOCEntry` whose `charOffsetUTF16 == chapter.globalStartUTF16` (skipping the synthetic "ÕēŹĶ©Ć" preamble, which was never tappable pre-fix). `ReaderTOCFactory.buildTOC` (case "txt") now calls this instead of its own decode + `TOCBuilder.forTXT`; `buildChapterIndexFromFullText` made internal (was private) so both paths share it. Navigation stays offset-based (`navigateToTOCTap` ŌåÆ `navigateToGlobalOffset`), so FIXED #234 is NOT regressed. Cross-ref #234, #282. **REDŌåÆGREEN**: new `ReaderTOCTXTAlignmentTests` (8) ŌĆö UTF-8 + GBK-with-ASCII-head alignment (TOC offset == reader chapter start), decode parity (`decodeTXTForTOC` == `decodeForDisplayAndSearch`), genuine >512KB competing-rule pattern shift, end-to-end production path (`ReaderTOCFactory.buildTOC` Ōåö `openChapterBased`), empty/no-pattern/single-chapter/preamble edges. RED demonstrated by reverting `decodeTXTForTOC` to the pre-fix decode ŌåÆ GBK ASCII-head tests fail (`entries.count ŌåÆ 0`, decode parity broken); GREEN after fix. Full `vreaderTests` suite 8208 tests PASS (iPhone 17 Pro Sim). **Gate-4 Codex audit** thread `019e74e9`, 2 rounds, ship-as-is ŌĆö round 1 found 2 Medium (tests didn't exercise the wired `ReaderTOCFactory.buildTOC` path; pattern-shift test wasn't a real competing-rule shift) + 3 Low, both Medium fixed (added production-path test + genuine two-rule-family shift), round 2 clean. Audit log `.claude/codex-audits/fix-bug-286-txt-toc-chapter-detection-audit.md`. GH: #1267 |

TWO more root causes, both in the windowed continuous-scroll path (`EPUBContinuousScroll*`): **(1) the boundary-signal parser dropped integer-`0` reports.** `EPUBScrollBoundarySignal.parse`'s int/double coercers tested `any is Bool` BEFORE the `NSNumber` branch; the live WKScriptMessage bridge turns every JS number into `NSNumber`, and `NSNumber(0)`/`NSNumber(1)` bridge-conflate with Swift `Bool`, so a real-book report of `visibleSpineIndex:0` + `intraFraction:0` (the reader sitting at/above section 0's `offsetTop` on the cover) was rejected ŌåÆ the window never extended off the cover. Fixed by reordering both coercers to test the `NSNumber` branch first and distinguish a true boolean only via `CFGetTypeID(n) == CFBooleanGetTypeID()` (`__NSCFBoolean` vs `__NSCFNumber`). **(2) eviction removed the chapter just loaded ahead of the reader.** Through a run of short front-matter sections the viewport spans >1 section, so the topmost-visible anchor LAGS the window's leading edge; the old `evictFarFromAnchor` then trimmed the far-from-anchor end = the section just materialized ahead of the reader, so the reader could never scroll into it and the window oscillated (device repro: stuck at window `[1,3]`, `scrollTop` pinned at max). Replaced with DIRECTIONAL `EPUBSpineWindow.evictTrailing(forward:maxSpan:)`: a forward extend trims only the trailing (`lo`) edge behind the reader and never the leading chapter (symmetric for backward); when the anchor sits within `maxSpan-1` of the trailing edge the window is left larger than `maxSpan` and shrinks back as the anchor advances. New unit coverage: `parse_acceptsIntegerZeroFields_liveReport`, `shortFrontMatter_laggingAnchor_extendForwardKeepsLeadingSection` / `ŌĆ”BackwardKeepsLeadingSection` (coordinator), full `evictTrailing` truth table (EPUBSpineWindow), all GREEN. Device slice (CU-free) on "The Half Second": continuous scroll now advances past the front matter into the chapters (window `hi` climbs `[0,2]ŌåÆ[1,3]ŌåÆ[2,5]/[2,6]`; the pre-fix build hard-pinned at `[1,3]`).
